Overview

This section describes the new version of Ixia BreakingPoint Representational State Transfer (REST) API functionality, BPS REST API v2.

REST API root URL

The Breaking Point Controller REST API root URL can be accessed at the same location with the Web Interface IP (System Controller IP) with the suffix: /bps/api/v2/core.
https://< System Controller IP >/bps/api/v2/core






Chassis Topology : 'topology'

Attributes:
- model [ string ]
- ixoslicensed [ bool ]
- ixos [ bool ]
- serialNumber [ string ]

Operations:

stopRun( runid[number])
Description: Stops the test run.
(runid) = Test RUN ID

reboot( board[number])
Description: Reboots the card. Only available for PerfectStorm and CloudStorm cards.

setCardMode( board[number], mode[number])
Description: Sets the card mode of a board.
(board) = Slot ID.
(mode) = The new mode: 10(BPS-L23), 7(BPS L4-7), 3(IxLoad), 11(BPS QT L2-3), 12(BPS QT L4-7)

setCardSpeed( board[number], speed[number])
Description: Sets the card speed of a board
(board) = Slot ID.
(speed) = The new speed.(the int value for 1G is 1000, 10G(10000), 40G(40000))

setCardFanout( board[number], fanid[number])
Description: Sets the card fanout of a board
(board) = Slot ID.
(fanid) = The fan type represented by an integer id. For CloudStorm: 0(100G), 1(40G), 2(25G), 3(10G), 4(50G). For PerfectStorm 40G: 0(40G), 1(10G). For PerfectStorm 100G: 0(100G), 1(40G), 2(10G)

setPerfAcc( board[number], perfacc[bool])
Description: Enables/Disables the performance acceleration for a BPS VE blade.
(board) = Slot ID.
(perfacc) = Boolean value: 'True' to enable the performance Acceleration and 'False' otherwise.

exportCapture( filepath[string], args[object])
Description: Exports a port capture from a test run.This operation can not be executed from the RESTApi Browser, it needs to be executed from a remote system through a REST call.
(filepath) = The local path where to save the exported object.
(args) = Export filters. The Possible values for: 'dir'(direction) are 'tx','rx','both';for 'sizetype' and 'starttype'(units for size and start) are 'megabytes' or 'frames'

reserve( reservation[list], force[bool] = False)

addPortNote( interface[object], note[string])
Description: Adds a note to given port.
(interface) = Slot and Port ID.
(note) = Note info.

run( modelname[string], group[number], allowMalware[bool] = False)
Description: Runs a Test.
(modelname) = Test Name to run
(group) = Group to run
(allowMalware) = Enable this option to allow malware in test.

unreserve( unreservation[list])

Super Flow : 'superflow'

Attributes:
- estimate_flows [ number ]
- weight [ number ]
- lockedBy [ string ]
- seed [ number ]
- label [ string ]
- percentBandwidth [ number ]
- percentFlows [ number ]
- createdOn [ object ]
- author [ string ]
- revision [ number ]
- estimate_bytes [ number ]
- createdBy [ string ]
- generated [ bool ]
- description [ string ]
- name [ string ]
- contentType [ enum ]
Description: BPS object type: Canned or Custom.

Operations:

removeFlow( id[number])
Description: Removes a flow from the current working SuperFlow.
(id) = The flow ID.

search( searchString[string], limit[string], sort[string], sortorder[string])
(searchString) = Search Super Flow name matching the string given.
(limit) = The limit of rows to return
(sort) = Parameter to sort by.
(sortorder) = The sort order (ascending/descending)

delete( name[string])
Description: Deletes a given Super Flow from the database.
(name) = The name of the Super Flow.

saveAs( name[string], force[bool])
Description: Saves the current working Application Profiles and gives it a new name.
(name) = The new name given for the current working Super Flow
(force) = Force to save the working Super Flow using the given name.

save( name[string] = null, force[bool] = True)
Description: Saves the working Super Flow using the current name
(name) = The name of the template that should be empty.
(force) = Force to save the working Super Flow with the same name.

removeAction( id[number])
Description: Removes an action from the current working SuperFlow.
(id) = The action ID.

load( template[string])
Description: Load an existing Super Flow and sets it as the current one.
(template) = The name of the existing Super Flow template

new( template[string] = null)
Description: Creates a new Super Flow.
(template) = The name of the template. In this case will be empty.

addAction( flowid[number], type[string], actionid[number], source[string])
Description: Adds an action to the current working SuperFlow
(flowid) = The flow id.
(type) = The type of the action definition.
(actionid) = The new action id.
(source) = The action source.

addHost( hostParams[object], force[bool])
Description: Add a host to the current working Superflow
(force) = The flow id.

addFlow( flowParams[object])
Description: Adds a flow to the current working SuperFlow
(flowParams) = The flow object to add.

getActionChoices( id[number])

Strike List : 'strikeList'

Attributes:
- createdOn [ object ]
- queryString [ string ]
- author [ string ]
- revision [ number ]
- createdBy [ string ]
- lockedBy [ string ]
- description [ string ]
- name [ string ]
- label [ string ]
- numStrikes [ number ]
- contentType [ enum ]
Description: BPS object type: Canned or Custom.

Operations:

delete( name[string])
Description: Deletes a given Strike List from the database.
(name) = The name of the Strike List to be deleted.

exportStrikeList( name[string], filepath[string])
Description: Exports the Strike List identified by its name and all of its dependenciesThis operation can not be executed from the RESTApi Browser, it needs to be executed from a remote system through a REST call.
(name) = The name of the strike list to be exported.
(filepath) = The local path where to save the exported object. The file should have .bap extension

search( searchString[string], limit[number] = 10, sort[string] = name, sortorder[string] = ascending)
(searchString) = Search strike list name matching the string given.
(limit) = The limit of rows to return
(sort) = Parameter to sort by. Default is by name.
(sortorder) = The sort order (ascending/descending). Default is ascending.

saveAs( name[string], force[bool])
Description: Saves the current working Strike List and gives it a new name.
(name) = The new name given for the current working Strike List
(force) = Force to save the working Strike List using the given name.

save( name[string] = null, force[bool] = True)
Description: Saves the current working Strike List using the current name
(name) = The name of the template. Default is empty.
(force) = Force to save the working Strike List with the same name.

add( strike[list])
Description: Adds a list of strikes to the current working Strike List.([{id: 'b/b/v/f'}, {id: 'aa/f/h'}])
(strike) = The list of strikes to add.

load( template[string])
Description: Load an existing Strike List and sets it as the current one.
(template) = The name of the Strike List template

new( template[string] = null)
Description: Creates a new Strike List.
(template) = The name of the template. In this case will be empty.

remove( strike[list])
Description: Removes a strike from the current working Strike List.([{id: 'bb/c/d'}, {id: 'aa/f/g'}])
(strike) = The list of strike ids to remove. The strike id is in fact the it's path.

importStrikeList( name[string], filename[string], force[bool])
Description: Imports a list of strikes residing in a file.
(name) = The name of the object being imported
(filename) = The file containing the object to be imported.
(force) = Force to import the file and the object having the same name will be replaced.

strikeList.strikes
Description: Strike object
Attributes:
- fileExtension [ string ]
- protocol [ string ]
- direction [ string ]
- severity [ string ]
- id [ string ]
- fileSize [ string ]
- category [ string ]
- name [ string ]
- path [ string ]
- variants [ number ]
- year [ string ]

strikeList.strikes.keyword
No Description.
Attributes:
- name [ string ]

strikeList.strikes.reference
No Description.
Attributes:
- value [ string ]
- label [ string ]
- type [ string ]

Administration : 'administration'


Operations:

logs( error[bool] = False, messages[bool] = False, web[bool] = False, all[bool] = False, audit[bool] = False, info[bool] = False, system[bool] = False, lines[number] = 20, drop[number] = 0)
(lines) = number lines to return
(drop) = number lines to drop

exportAllTests( filepath[string])
Description: Exports everything including test models, network configurations and others from system.This operation can not be executed from the RESTApi Browser, it needs to be executed from a remote system through a REST call.
(filepath) = The local path where to save the compressed file with all the models. The path must contain the file name and extension (.tar.gz): '/d/c/f/AllTests.tar.gz'

administration.systemSettings
Description: BPS system settings
Attributes:
- createdOn [ object ]
- author [ string ]
- revision [ number ]
- createdBy [ string ]
- lockedBy [ string ]
- description [ string ]
- label [ string ]
- contentType [ enum ]
Description: BPS object type: Canned or Custom.

(value) = The new value for setting.

administration.atiLicensing
Description: ATI License. It retrieves information about the ATI Licenses installed on a BPS Hardware setup.

Operations:

importAtiLicense( filename[string], name[string])
Description: Imports an ATI License file (.lic) on a hardware platform. This operation is NOT recommended to be used on BPS Virtual platforms.
(filename) = import file path
(name) = the name of the license file

Results : 'results'

Attributes:
- content [ string ]
- datasetvals [ string ]
- name [ string ]

Operations:

getHistoricalResultSize( runid[number], componentid[string], group[string])
(runid) = The test run id
(componentid) = The component identifier
(group) = The data group or one of the BPS component main groups. The group name can be get by executing the operation 'getGroups' from results node

getGroups( name[string], dynamicEnums[bool] = True, includeOutputs[bool] = True)
Description: Returns main groups of statistics for a single BPS Test Component. These groups can be used then in requesting statistics values from the history of a test run.
(name) = BPS Component name. This argument is actually the component type which can be get from 'statistics' table

getHistoricalSeries( runid[number], componentid[string], dataindex[number], group[string])
Description: Returns stats series for a given component group stat output for a given timestamp
(runid) = The test identifier
(componentid) = The component identifier. Each component has an id and can be get loading the testand checking it's components info
(dataindex) = The table index, equivalent with timestamp.
(group) = The data group or one of the BPS component main groups. The group name can be get by executing the operation 'getGroups' from results node.

Attributes:

- author [ string ]
- revision [ number ]
- createdBy [ string ]
- lockedBy [ string ]
- description [ string ]
- label [ string ]
- contentType [ enum ]
Description: BPS object type: Canned or Custom.

Strikes : 'strikes'

Attributes:
- fileExtension [ string ]
- protocol [ string ]
- direction [ string ]
- severity [ string ]
- id [ string ]
- fileSize [ string ]
- category [ string ]
- name [ string ]
- path [ string ]
- variants [ number ]
- year [ string ]

Operations:

search( searchString[string], limit[number] = 10, sort[string] = name, sortorder[string] = ascending, offset[number] = 0)
Description: Searches a strike inside all BPS strike database.To list all the available strikes, leave the arguments empty.
(searchString) = The string used as a criteria to search a strike by.Example: 'strike_name', 'year:2019', 'path:strikes/xml..'
(limit) = The limit of rows to return. Use empty string or empty box to get all the available strikes.
(sort) = Parameter to sort by.
(sortorder) = The sort order (ascending/descending)
(offset) = The offset to begin from. Default is 0.

Working Test Model : 'testmodel'

Attributes:
- result [ string ]
- lastrun [ object ]
- lockedBy [ string ]
- label [ string ]
- lastrunby [ string ]
- network [ string ]
- createdOn [ object ]
- author [ string ]
- revision [ number ]
- duration [ number ]
- createdBy [ string ]
- description [ string ]
- name [ string ]
- contentType [ enum ]
Description: BPS object type: Canned or Custom.

Operations:

stopRun( runid[number])
Description: Stops the test run.
(runid) = Test RUN ID

realTimeStats( runid[number], rtsgroup[string], numSeconds[number], numDataPoints[number] = 1)
Description: Retrieves the real time statistics for the running test, by giving the run id.
(runid) = Test RUN ID
(rtsgroup) = Real Time Stats group name. Values for this can be get from 'statistics' node, inside 'statNames' from each component at 'realtime Group' key/column. Examples: l7STats, all, bpslite, summary, clientStats etc.
(numSeconds) = The number of seconds. If negative, means from the end
(numDataPoints) = The number of data points, the default is 1.

delete( name[string])
Description: Deletes a given Test Model from the database.
(name) = The name of the Test Model.

add( name[string], component[string], type[string], active[bool])
Description: Adds a new test component to the current working test model
(name) = Component Name
(component) = Component template, preset.
(type) = Component Type: appsim, sesionsender ..
(active) = Set component enable (by default is active) or disable

importModel( name[string], filename[string], force[bool])
Description: Imports a test model, given as a file. This operation can not be executed from the RESTApi Browser, it needs to be executed from a remote system through a REST call.
(name) = The name of the object being imported
(filename) = The file containing the object
(force) = Force to import the file and the object having the same name will be replaced.

saveAs( name[string], force[bool])
Description: Saves the current working Test Model under specified name.
(name) = The new name given for the current working Test Model
(force) = Force to save the working Test Model using a new name.

save( name[string] = null, force[bool] = True)
Description: Saves the working Test Model using the current name. No need to configure. The current name is used.
(name) = The name of the template that should be empty.
(force) = Force to save the working Test Model with the same name.

remove( id[string])
Description: Removes a component from the current working Test Model.
(id) = The component id.

clone( template[string], type[string], active[bool])
Description: Clones a component in the current working Test Model
(template) = The ID of the test component to clone.
(type) = Component Type: appsim, sesionsender ..
(active) = Set component enable (by default is active) or disable

run( modelname[string], group[number], allowMalware[bool] = False)
Description: Runs a Test.
(modelname) = Test Name to run
(group) = Group to run
(allowMalware) = Enable this option to allow malware in test.

exportModel( name[string], attachments[bool], filepath[string], runid[number] = null)
Description: Exports a wanted test model by giving its name or its test run id.This operation can not be executed from the RESTApi Browser, it needs to be executed from a remote system through a REST call.
(name) = The name of the test model to be exported.
(attachments) = True if object attachments are needed.
(filepath) = The local path where to save the exported object.
(runid) = Test RUN ID

load( template[string])
Description: Load an existing test model template.
(template) = The name of the template testmodel

new( template[string] = null)
Description: Creates a new Test Model
(template) = The name of the template. In this case will be empty.

search( searchString[string], limit[string], sort[string], sortorder[string])
(searchString) = Search test name matching the string given.
(limit) = The limit of rows to return
(sort) = Parameter to sort by: 'createdOn'/'timestamp'/'bandwidth'/'result'/'lastrunby'/'createdBy'/'interfaces'/'testLabType'
(sortorder) = The sort order: ascending/descending

testmodel.component@type:layer2
Description: Bit Blaster: This component measures the raw throughput of a device. It sends valid layer 2 Ethernet frames with contrived content, and measures whether the frames reach their intended destination.
Attributes:
- slowStart [ bool ]
Description: Slow Start: This parameter specifies if the test component is allowed to send a small amount of traffic at the beginning of the test before ramping up to the full rate of the test. This will allow routing DUTs to warm their ARP cache and switching DUTs to identify which port to send test-generated traffic. The slow start traffic is sent at rate of approximately 100 to 500 packets/second. This traffic is usually sent in the reverse direction to advertise the MAC addresses of the target devices to the DUT.
- maxStreams [ number ]
Description: Maximum Stream Count: This override parameter sets the maximum number of streams to use for this component. It allows the user to reduce the unique stream count to a subset of the total streams possible with the network neighborhood configuration. Note that with the Routing Robot component, users are already able to limit the number of streams by specifying minimum and maximum IP address range values. The Maximum Stream Count sets the number of rightmost bits which change in a address (MAC and/or IP). For switched networks, the patterns of all 1's is not used in the varied bit fields. For routed networks, the all 1's pattern, the all 0's pattern, and the router gateway addresses are not used. An example: in a routed network neighborhood that has a network mask of 8, we would like to limit the # of streams to 32 or less. Set the Max Stream Count in the component to 32. This indicates that the 5 most right bits can change (2**5 == 32), and since the neighborhood is routed, there will be 29 unique streams generated. If a non-power of 2 value is specified in Maximum Stream Count, the value used will be lowered down value of the next power of 2. For example if 31 is specified, the value implied will be 16 indicating that the 4 bits of rightmost addresses will be allowed to change. This component requires that the 3 rightmost bits in the address are modifiable. Therefore the minimum value of this parameter is 8. (min=8, max=16777216, default=64, )
- bidirectional [ bool ]
Description: Bidirectional: Originate traffic from both the client and server interfaces. (default=false, )
- slowStartFps [ number ]
Description: Slow Start Rate: This parameter sets the rate of the slow start traffic. The rate is specified in the number of frames per second. A setting of zero will use the default of 32 frames per second. The initialization phase will include the time required to send packets on the streams configured for this test. The maximum stream count parameter divided by the frames per second rate will give an estimate of how much time will be required for the initialization phase. Please note that large stream counts may cause long initialization periods. (min=0, max=1000000, default=32, )
- delayStart [ string ]
Description: Delay Start: Establishes the amount of time before a test component begins. (min=00:00:00, default=00:00:00, )

testmodel.component.payload
Description: Payload : This parameter defines the contents of the data portion of each packet in the test. Where this data is inserted depends on the test type. For Bit Blaster, this parameter defines the payload after the Ethernet header. For Routing Robot, this is the UDP payload. For Session Sender, this parameter defines the contents of a TCP segment. When the Payload type is specified as '0', data has all bits cleared. When the Payload type is specified as '1', data has all bits set. When the Payload type is specified as 'Random', data is filled with random values. When the Payload type is specified as 'Increment', data is filled with ascending values based on the data width setting. When the Payload type is specified as 'Decrement', data is filled with descending values based on the data width setting. When the Payload type is specified as 'User Defined', data is input in standard hexdecimal notation. If the user specifies less data in the Data field than the specified frame or packet size, this data is repeated in the payload. Data Width: when Payload type is 'Increment' or 'Decrement', this value indicates the width (in bits) of the data values being manipulated.
Attributes:
- dataWidth [ enum ]
Description: Data Width : (default=eight, )
- data [ object ]
Description: User Defined Data :
- type [ enum ]
Description: Type :

testmodel.component.sizeDist
Description: Size Distribution: These parameters define the frame/packet size(s) generated by the test component. Size Distribution Unit: 'Frame' indicates the 14 byte Ethernet header and 4 byte Ethernet frame CRC is included in the specifed size, 'Packet' indicates the Ethernet header/CRC is not included in the specified size. Size Distribution Type: 'Constant' indicates that all generated frames/packets will be the size in the Minimum Frame/Packet Size field, 'Mix' indicates up to 10 different frame/packet sizes will be used with a weighting factor per size, 'Random' indicates that frame/packet sizes should be chosen randomly between Minimum and Maximum Frame/Packet Size's, inclusive, changing once every second during test execution, 'Range' indicates that frame/packet sizes should start at Minimum Frame/Packet Size field and increase up to the Maximum Frame/Packet Size. Minimum/Maximum Frame/Packet Size: min/max size of frames/packets (in bytes). Values of 64 to 9216 are supported for frames. Values of 46 to 9198 are supported for packets. Please review for the Overheads section below for more information about minimum frame/packet sizes. Increment N Bytes: when Size Distribution Type is 'Range', this value indicates the "step" amount (in bytes) to incrementally change the size during the course of the test. When this value is positive, the test will begin with frames/packets that are the Minimum Frame/Packet Size in size. Values of -128 to 128 are supported. Every N Seconds: when Size Distribution Type is 'Range', this value indicates the delay (in seconds) between frame/packet size changes. Values of 1 to 3600 are supported. Overheads: The Bit Blaster and Routing Robot components use the last 16 bytes (before the Ethernet CRC) of the packet/frame for hardware signature verification. The overheads of VLAN tags, IPv4 or IPv6 headers (including option fields and extension headers) and upper layer templates (such as UDP/TCP headers) all reserve space that must be factored into the minimum packet/frame size required. The 16 byte signature field is used in all configurations and an error warning will result if not enough space is reserved for the hardware signature in the packet/frame as defined by the test parameters and Network Neighborhood.

testmodel.component.payloadAdvanced
Description: Advanced Options - Payload : These parameters allow placement of a User Defined Field (UDF) into the payload data. The UDF can either be an incrementing counter or byte pattern, which overwrites the existing payload data so the packet length is unchanged. Where this data is placed depends on the test type. In this test component, the payload begins after the Ethernet header. UDF Mode: 'Counter' will insert a 32 bit wide counter value which increments every frame. 'Random' will insert a sequence of random values, while 'Increment'/'Decrement' will insert a sequence of incrementing or decrementing values. Random, Increment and Decrement modes specify 8, 16, or 32-bit width specified by UDF data width. 'Disabled' will not use the UDF in the test. UDF Offset: indicates the number of bytes from the beginning of the payload to place the UDF data. Values of 0 to 9201 are supported, with 0 being the first byte of the payload. UDF Length: indicates the UDF length (in bytes). Values of 1 to 9202 are supported. UDF Data Width: when UDF Mode is 'Increment' or 'Decrement', this value indicates the width (in bits) of the data values being manipulated.
Attributes:

Description: UDF Data Width : (default=eight, )

Description: UDF Offset : (min=0, max=9201, )
- udfMode [ enum ]
Description: UDF Mode :
- udfLength [ number ]
Description: UDF Length : (min=1, max=9202, )

testmodel.component.advanced
Description: Advanced Options: Ethernet Type Field: 'Constant' indicates the Ethernet Type Value should be placed in the Ethernet 'length/type' field of each packet, 'Length' indicates the packet length should be used (valid only when packet sizes are 1500-or-less bytes in length; otherwise 'Constant' is implied). Ethernet Type Value: when Ethernet Type Field is set to 'Constant' (or when packet sizes are more than 1500 bytes in length), this indicates the value to be placed in the 'length/type' field of the Layer 2 header. Values of 2E through FFFF (hexadecimal) are currently supported, except for VLAN TPID values (8100, 88a8, 9100, 9200, 9300), which are not supported.

testmodel.component.rateDist
Description: Data Rate: These parameters define the maximum transmit data rate that the test will use per-interface. When specifying a rate in megabits / second, the ethernet inter-packet gap is included in the rate value. Therefore, the amount of usable data 'on the wire' will be less than the rate value, depending on frame / packet size. Data Rate Unit: defines the units, either 'Frames / Second' or 'Megabits / Second' that the Minimum/Maximum data rates (below) represent. Data Rate Type: 'Constant' indicates that all generated traffic will be at the data rate specified by the Minimum data rate field, 'Range' indicates that data rate should start at either the Minimum or Maximum data rate and increase or decrease over the course of the test (see Increment field below), 'Random' indicates that data rate should be chosen randomly between Minimum and Maximum data rates, inclusive, changing once every second during test execution. Minimum/Maximum data rate: min/max data rate. Values of 1 to 1488095 (1 Gigabit ports) or 14880952 (10/40/100 Gigabit ports) are supported for 'Frames / Second'. Values of 1 to 1000 (1 Gigabit ports) or 10000 (10/40/100 Gigabit ports) are supported for 'Megabits / Second'. * Increment N units: when Data Rate Type is 'Range', this value indicates the "step" amount (in frames / second or Megabits / Second, based on the data rate unit value) to incrementally change the rate during the course of the test. When this value is positive, the test will begin at the Minimum data rate as its rate. When this value is negative, the test will begin with the Maximum data rate as its rate. Values of -10000 to 10000 are supported. Ramp Type: When Data Rate Type is 'Range', this value indicates what to do when reaching the maximum or minimum range value. The setting, 'wrap' will reset the data rate to the initial rate value at the start of the test and 'limit' will hold the terminating data rate till the end of the test. Every N Seconds: when Data Rate Type is 'Range', this value indicates the delay (in seconds) between rate changes. Values of 1 to 3600 are supported. *: Actual transmit rate may vary by up to 2% from configured value, due to 5 nanosecond granularity within the interpacket timer. The effect will be most pronounced at packet sizes of 100 bytes or less.
Attributes:
- min [ number ]
Description: Minimum Data Rate : (min=1, default=1000, )
- increment [ number ]
Description: Increment N Units/Period : (min=-10000, max=10000, default=0, )
- unit [ enum ]

- rate [ number ]
Description: Every N Seconds : (min=1, max=3600, default=1, )
- max [ number ]
Description: Maximum Data Rate : (min=1, default=1000, )

Description: Data Rate Ramp : (default=wrap, )

testmodel.component.sessions
Description: Session/Super Flow Configuration : Maximum Super Flows Per Second: This parameter defines the maximum number of Super Flows that will be instantiated per second. If there is one flow per Super Flow, as in Session Sender, this is functionally equivalent to the sum of TCP and UDP flows per second. In cases where there are multiple flows per Super Flow, you may see a varying number of effective flows per second. While there is a limit of 1,000,000 sessions per second per component, be sure to consider several factors when setting this parameter. First, there must be adequate bandwidth allocated to the test via the Rate Distribution parameter to achieve a particular number of sessions per second. For instance, a new TCP session requires approximately 150 bytes to establish when originating out a particular interface. Second, the ramp up duration generally should be 1 second or longer for higher numbers of sessions per second. This ensures that the test has some phase where test bandwidth is exclusively dedicated to setting up sessions. Maximum Simultaneous Active Flows This parameter defines the maximum number of flows that can be active at a time. Active flows includes all flows other than the TCP flows that are currently aging (in the TIME_WAIT state). A value of 0 disables this limit. Maximum Simultaneous Super Flows: This parameter defines the maximum simultaneous Super Flows that will exist concurrently during the test duration. If there is one flow per Super Flow, as in Session Sender, this is functionally equivalent to the sum of TCP and UDP flows. In cases where there are multiple flows per Super Flow, you may see a varying number of effective simultaneous flows. This value defines a shared resource between different test components, and is limited to 60,000,000. In other words, the total maximum simultaneous sessions for all components in a test must be less than or equal to 60,000,000. Unlimited Super Flow Open Rate: This parameter determines globally how fast sessions are opened. If set to true, sessions will be opened as fast as possible. This setting is useful for tests where the session rate is not the limiting factor for a test's performance. Note: this setting may produce session open rates faster than the global limit. Unlimited Super Flow Close Rate: This parameter determines how fast sessions are closed. If set to false, session close rate will mirror the session open rate. If set to true, sessions will be closed as fast as possible. Target Minimum Super Flows Per Second: This parameter specifies a minimum number of sessions that the test must open in order to pass in the final results. This is an aid for the user to define pass/fail criteria for a particular test. This parameter does not affect the network traffic of the test in any way. Target Minimum Simultaneous Super Flows: This parameter specifies a minimum number of sessions per second that the test must open in order to pass in the final results. This is an aid for the user to define pass/fail criteria for a particular test. This parameter does not affect the network traffic of the test in any way. Target Number of Successful matches: This parameter specifies the minimum number of successful matches required to pass in the final results. This is an aid for the user to define pass/fail criteria for a particular test. This parameter does not affect the network traffic of the test in any way. Engine Selection: This parameter selects the type of engine with which to run the test component. Select "Advanced" to enable the default, full-featured engine. Select "Simple" to enable a simpler, higher-performance, stateless engine. Performance Emphasis: This parameter adjusts whether the advanced engine's flow scheduler favors opening new sessions, sending on existing sessions, or a mixture of both. Select "Throughput" to emphasize sending data on existing sessions. Select "Simultaneous Sessions" to emphazise opening new sessions. Select "Balanced" to emphasize both equally - this is the default setting. Note:Ramp-up phases automatically emphasize Sessions, ramp-down phases emphasize Throughput. Resource Allocation Override: This parameter allows the user to override the amount of CPU and other resources allocated to this test component. Normally, the system estimates the amount of resources required by a particular component based on various heuristics. Sometimes, manual tuning is required for optimal performance. The value indicates the amount of resouces to use on a single processor. This parameter is best used when all components are configured for Auto or all components have an override value specified. If the sum of all resources of all components is less than 100%, then this value is treated as a weight, and any extra resources are distributed evenly according to the weight value. Statistic Detail: This parameter adjusts the level of statistics to be collected. Decreasing the number of statistics collected can increase performance and allow for targeted reporting. Select "Maximum" to enable all possible statistics Select "Application Only" to enable only Application statistics (L7) Select "Transport Only" to enable only Transport statistics (L4/L3) Select "Minimum" to disable most statistics
Attributes:
- max [ number ]
Description: Maximum Simultaneous Super Flows : (min=1, )
- closeFast [ bool ]
Description: Unlimited Super Flow Close Rate : (default=false, )
- engine [ enum ]
Description: Engine Selection:
- statDetail [ enum ]
Description: Statistic Detail:
- targetPerSecond [ number ]
Description: Target Minimum Super Flows Per Second : (min=0, max=1000000, )
- openFast [ bool ]
Description: Unlimited Super Flow Open Rate : (default=false, )
- targetMatches [ number ]
Description: Target Number of Successful Matches : (min=0, default=0, )
- maxActive [ number ]
Description: Maximum Simultaneous Active Flows : (min=0, default=0, )
- allocationOverride [ enum ]
Description: Resource Allocation Override : (default=auto, )
- maxPerSecond [ object ]
Description: Maximum Super Flows Per Second : (min=0, )
- target [ number ]
Description: Target Minimum Simultaneous Flows : (min=0, max=30000000, )
- emphasis [ enum ]
Description: Performance Emphasis :

testmodel.component.srcPortDist
Description: Source Port : These parameters control the distribution of source ports for TCP connections. Note that setting these parameters to a constant or narrow range can severely limit the available number of tuples that the test component can use for setting up new connections. In the event that the available tuple space is too limited, the test may not achieve the specified number of connections. If this happens, simply expand the range of source or destination ports that the test can use. Constant specifies that the same port will be used for every flow tuple. Range specifies that the ports will be used sequentually, from min to max. This is a best-effort, since other test parameters might cause ports to be reused or skipped. Random specifies no ordering. Ports will be chosen randomly between min to max. Note: Some application protocols enforce source port allocations that can override this parameter as well, depending on the test component and configuration.
Attributes:
- min [ number ]
Description: Minimum Port Number : (min=0, max=65535, )
- max [ number ]
Description: Maximum Port Number : (min=0, max=65535, )
- type [ enum ]
Description: Port Distribution Type :

testmodel.component.rampUpProfile
Description: Ramp Up Profile : Specify how the connection rate should be controlled during the ramp up phase Ramp Up Profile Type: Specifies whether the connection establishment rate should be * Calculated: a constant rate, calculated as the maximum number of sessions divided by ramp up time. This is the default behavior and attempts to reach the overall maximum number of connections over the course of the entire ramp up time. The other parameters are disabled in this mode. This affects ramp-down as well when 'Calculated' mode is specified. * Exact: the configured session rate is honored during the ramp-up phase * Stair Step: a stair-step ramp-up profile defined by user parameters. This also disables the 'Calculated' mode for ramp-down Minimum Connection Rate: Specifies the connection establishment rate to be used at the start of the ramp up phase when not in Calculated mode. Maximum Connection Rate: Limits the maxium connection establishment rate for the ramp up phase when not in Calculated mode. Increment N Connections Per Second: Increases connection establishment rate by this value at every interval when not in Calculated mode. Fixed Time Interval: The interval at which connection establishment rate will be changed when not in Calculated mode.
Attributes:
- min [ number ]
Description: Min Connection Rate : (min=1, max=4000000, )
- increment [ number ]

- max [ number ]
Description: Max Connection Rate : (min=1, max=4000000, )
- interval [ string ]

- type [ enum ]
Description: Ramp Up Profile Type :

testmodel.component.rampDist
Description: Session Ramp Distribution : The session ramp distribution defines 3 distinct phases within a test. The ramp up phase defines a duration where only new TCP sessions are established, but not closed. Other traffic (UDP/ARP/ICMP) is unaffected during this time. This phase is useful to setup a large number of TCP sessions in a short period of time. During the ramp steady-state phase, the test will maintain up to the maximum number of sessions specified open simultaneously. Sessions will open, close and send data as well. During the ramp down phase, any sessions that are open will attempt to close. Ramp Up Behavior: During the ramp up phase, TCP sessions are only opened, but no data is sent. This is useful for quickly setting up a large number of sessions without wasting bandwidth. This parameter defines what the test actually does during the ramp up phase. Note: after the ramp up phase, all sessions will fully open, even if the ramp up behavior was set to something other than "Full Open". "Full Open" - The full TCP handshake is performed on open "Full Open + Data" - Same as full, but start sending data "Full Open + Data + Full Close" - Same as full + data, but also do a full close for completed sessions. "Full Open + Data + Close with Reset" - Same as full + data, but also initiate the TCP close with a RST. "Half Open" - Same as full, but omit the final ACK "SYN Only" - Only SYN packets are sent "Data Only" - Only PSH data packets are sent, with no TCP state machine processing. This mode is not compatible with SSL nor with Conditional Requests. Any flow using SSL will send no packets. SYN Only Retry Mode: Defines the behavior of the TCP Retry Mechanism when dealing with the initial SYN packet of a flow, the following modes are permitted: "Continous" - Continue sending SYN packets, even if we have ran out of retries (Retry Count). "Continous with new session" - Same as "Continous", except we change the initial sequence number every "Retry Count" loop(s). "Obey Retry" - Send no more than "Retry Count" initial SYN packets. NOTE: This option is only active during the ramp up phase and only if the "Ramp Up Behavior" is set to "SYN Only"! Steady-State Behavior: This parameter defines the test behavior during the steady-state phase. This setting is useful for examining connection tracking and timeout behavior of a device under test, as well as maintaining a steady load with a sustained number of simultaneous sessions. "Open and Close Sessions" - sessions are closed as they finish sending data and new ones opened in their place. "Open and Close with Reset" - initiate the TCP close with a RST This bypasses the TCP close state machine. "Open and Close with Reset Response" - respond to a FIN with a RST This bypasses the TCP TIME_WAIT state. "Hold Sessions Open" - sessions are not closed as they finish sending data Ramp Down Behavior: During the Ramp Down phase, no new sessions will be established. As existing sessions complete during the Ramp Down phase, they will be closed in the manner specified by this setting. If a session does not complete before the Ramp Down time has expired, it will remain open. "Full Close" - The full TCP session close is performed "Half Close" - Same as above, but omit the final ACK "Reset" - initiate the TCP close with a RST This bypasses the TCP close state machine. "Reset Response" - respond to a FIN with a RST This bypasses the TCP TIME_WAIT state. #lt;pre#gt; c o s __________maxSessions__________ n e /| |\ c s / | | \ u s / | | \ r i / | | \ r o / | | \ e n / | | \ n s /______|_____________________________|______\ t ramp up ramp steady-state time ramp down time time #lt;/pre#gt;
Attributes:
- downBehavior [ enum ]
Description: Ramp Down Behavior : (default=full, )
- up [ string ]
Description: Ramp Up Duration : (min=0, max=300:00:00, default=00:00:01, )
- upBehavior [ enum ]
Description: Ramp Up Behavior : (default=full, )
- synRetryMode [ enum ]
Description: SYN Only Retry Mode : (default=continuous, )
- down [ string ]
Description: Ramp Down Time Interval : (min=0, max=300:00:00, default=00:00:01, )
- steadyBehavior [ enum ]
Description: Steady-State Behavior : (default=cycle, )
- steady [ string ]
Description: Steady-State Time Interval : (min=0, max=300:00:00, default=00:00:30, )

testmodel.component.ip
Description: IPv4 Configuration : Time To Live (TTL): The maximum bound on the number-of-hops that an IP datagram can exist in an internet system before it is dropped. Values of 0 through 255 (decimal) are supported. Type of Service (TOS)/Differentiated Services Code Point(DSCP): Configures the 8-bit combined TOS/DSCP (also sometimes called DS) field used for all IP packets. Specifies how IP packets are handled across the internet. Values of 0 through FF (hexadecimal) are supported.
Attributes:
- tos [ object ]
Description: TOS/DSCP : (min=0, max=ff, )
- ttl [ number ]
Description: TTL : (min=0, max=255, )

testmodel.component.loadprofile
Description: Load Profile : Load Profiles provide you with granular control over the attributes of the ramp-up, steady-state, and ramp down phases that occur during the test. For each phase, you can set the data rate, session rate, session behavior, and the maximum number of simultaneous sessions. If a Load Profile is enabled for the test, then you will not need to configure the following parameters from the Parameters tab: Data Rate Distribution.Data Rate Scope Data Rate Distribution.Data Rate Unit Data Rate Distribution.Data Rate Type Data Rate Distribution.Minimum Data Rate Data Rate Distribution.Maximum Data Rate Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Up Behavior Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Up Seconds Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Steady-State Behavior Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Steady-State Seconds Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Down Behavior Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Down Seconds Session Configuration.Maximum Simultaneous Sessions Session Configuration.Maximum Sessions Per Second The test will retrieve these parameter configurations from the Load Profile. Some Load Profiles will require that you have a specific preset selected for the test. If these Load Profiles do not use the required preset, then the test may not yield the expected stair case behavior. Please note that you must select the preset for the test before you select the Load Profile. To select a preset, go to the Test Editor screen; click the Presets tab; select the appropriate preset; and click the Apply Changes button. Once you have done this, you can go to the Parameters tab and choose the Load Profile. As it is, the BreakingPoint Maximum Sessions Per Second Load Profile will not provide the expected staircase behavior for the test. To simulate staircase behavior, you will need to use the Maximum Possible preset, and you will need to change the values for the following parameters on the Parameters tab: - Payload Size Distribution.Distribution Type must be constant. - Payload Size Distribution.Minimum Size must be 1. - Payload.Type must be 1. - Payload Packets Per Session must be 1.
Attributes:
- name [ string ]
- label [ string ]

testmodel.component.prng
Description: Pseudo-random Number Generator Options : These options provide a way to initialize the random number generator at the beginning of the test. Tests with the same seed and offset would use the same pseudorandom data. This makes it possible to have repeatable tests. Choosing a non-zero seed causes stackscrambler to run within a single-thread, this slows performance, but improves repeatability.
Attributes:
- seed [ number ]
Description: Seed for the Generator : (min=0, max=4294967295, )
- offset [ number ]
Description: Offset into the Seed : (min=0, max=4294967295, )

testmodel.component.tcp
Description: TCP Configuration : Maximum Segment Size (MSS): The maximum segment size that is advertised during session setup. A value of '0' will automatically configure an optimal MSS for the chosen network, MTU and transport settings. Aging Time: The time, expressed in seconds, that an actively-closed TCP connection will remain in the flow table in the TIME_WAIT state after closing. Flows in the TIME_WAIT count against simultaneous sessions, but do not generate any traffic. Setting this to a high value can cause traffic to slow over time. This setting is useful for matching the flow tracking policy of the DUT. Reset at End: Indicates whether a test should reset all existing TCP connections at the end. If enabled, all TCP connections will reset if the test either ends naturally or is cancelled. Note, RST packets received via this option will not be counted as received at the application layer in reports, only at the TCP and IP layers. Retry Count: Defines the number of retries before a connection is considered errored-out and is canceled by the TCP stack. Retry Quantum: Defines the minimum number of milliseconds between retrying a send. As the number of retries increases, this quantum is doubled for each retry. Delay ACKs: Determines whether to delay ACKing of TCP segments. If enabled, segments are ACKed on the next send, rather than separately on receive. Delayed ACKs ms: Define the minimum number of miliseconds before sending ACK for received segments. Must not exceed the Retry Quantum in order to avoid useless retransmits. A value of "0" will enable a dynamic mechanism that adjusts the value based on the receive window and the retry quantum. Disable Piggy-back Data on ACK (experimental): Forces the transmitting side to send an empty ACK (no data) before starting to send data packets (instead of piggy-backing data on the ACK packets). ACK every N (experimental): This value will force sending an ACK at least every N TCP segments. Default value is 0, which lets the conventional Delay ACKs mechanism work as usual. Note: Forcibly changing the ACK sending pattern is not RFC compliant and can result in unexpected behavior. The TCP protocol itself limits the flexibility of the 'ACK every N' mechanism. In some scenarios we must send an ACK no matter what; this implies that we might send some ACKs earlier that some would expect if the receiver's window fills, the flow ends or the TCP burst ends. In order to improve the pattern's consistency, the recommendation is to set the value for "ACK every N" as a divisor of "TCP Segment Credit" value. Initial Receive Window: Determines the size of the initial receive window for a new connection, in bytes. Internally, the receive window is managed as a number segments of MSS size, so the actual value used is truncated to an MSS multiple. The internal minimum initial value is 1 * MSS. TCP Window Scale: This value will allow the tcp connection to negotiate the window scale option as per RFC1323. The value set can be from 0-14 with 0 being disabled. The value set will be the maximum window size that the connection will attempt to negotiate. The window scale factor is the number of bits by which to shift the window size. Send and receive windows are negotiated separately based on the configuration of the equipment at each end. Dynamic Receive Window Size Determines if the size of the receive window should be increased during test run. The receive window size is increased until it reaches the maximum value (65535 * 2 ^ window_scale_factor). If delayed ACK is enabled, the receive window size is doubled on window full (the remaining receive window size is smaller than MSS), otherwise the receive window size is increased by MSS with each received segment. Add Segment Timestamps: In order to measure inter-packet latency, the stack can add a TCP timestamp option. This expands the size of the TCP header by 12 bytes to 32 bytes, and decreases the effective MSS by 12 bytes. No frame latencies are recorded by the component if this is disabled. Piggy-back Data on 3-way Handshake: Determines whether to add Data to the client ACK packet of the TCP handshake. Piggy-back Data on Shutdown: Determines whether to add Data to the client FIN packet of the TCP shutdown. Initial Congestion Window: Determines the size of the initial congestion window. A value of '0' means the TCP slow start is disabled (the congestion window is not used). Raw Flags: Allows the user to force TCP flags to a particular value, as a decimal number. Add values together to get a combination of TCP flags. Examples: 1 = FIN 2 = SYN 4 = RST 8 = PSH 16 = ACK 32 = URG 64 = ECE 128 = CWR 18 = SYN|ACK -1 Disables this feature (Default). Note: this feature breaks the TCP state machine. Connect Delay: Defines the minimum number of milliseconds between the TCP SYN and SYN|ACK and between the SYN|ACK and the final ACK in the 3-way SYN exchange. The TCP connect delay will end up being twice this number. TCP Keepalive Timer: Number of milliseconds until we send a TCP Keep Alive packet. If a TCP connection is in a "delayed" state, we will send a keep alive ACK every N seconds (N being the value you indicate in this field), zero disables this feature. A connection would be considered "delayed" in one of two ways, either by a SuperFlow stopping on an actual "Client: Delay" or "Server: Delay" action, or if a TCP connection is being held open by selecting the option "Hold Sessions Open" in a "Steady-State" ramp frame. Be advised, the first keep alive packet will be sent at a different interval. If you take this value, divide in half, then add the "TCP Retry Count" from above, that will be the number of milliseconds we will wait until sending the first keep alive packet. For example, if you set this value to 10000 ms and the Retry Counter to 2000 ms, the first keep alive will be sent 7000 ms from being "delayed" (10000/2 + 2000 = 7000) and then every 10000 milliseconds until the end of the flow or it is closed. 4-way Close: When a FIN packet is received, this option simulates the TCP half-close ability. Please be aware that no data can be sent/received after the connection is closed. Send PSH with all data segments: If enabled, every data segment will have the PSH flag on. Otherwise, the behaviour will stay default. SYN data padding size: This field only works on the SYN-ONLY mode, that enables TCP SYN Flood functionality. With "SYN data padding size" we can select the payload size of the data attached to the SYN packets in the SYN-ONLY mode.
Attributes:
- syn_data_padding [ number ]
Description: SYN data padding size: (min=0, max=1440, default=0, )
- delay_acks [ bool ]
Description: Delay ACKs :
- retry_quantum_ms [ number ]
Description: Retry Quantum : (min=1, max=2000, )
- tcp_connect_delay_ms [ number ]
Description: Connect Delay : (min=0, max=10, default=0, )
- reset_at_end [ bool ]
Description: Reset at End :
- disable_ack_piggyback [ bool ]
Description: Disable Piggy-back data on ACK (experimental) :
- tcp_icw [ number ]
Description: Initial Congestion Window : (min=0, max=16, default=0, )
- aging_time_data_type [ enum ]
Description: Aging Time Data Type: (default=aging_time_data_type_sc, )
- delay_acks_ms [ number ]
Description: Delayed ACKs ms : (min=0, max=500, default=0, )
- aging_time [ number ]
Description: Aging Time : (min=0, max=120, )
- tcp_window_scale [ number ]
Description: TCP Window Scale : (min=0, max=14, )
- dynamic_receive_window_size [ bool ]
Description: Dynamic Receive Window Size : (default=true, )
- add_timestamps [ bool ]
Description: Add Segment Timestamps :
- ack_every_n [ number ]
Description: ACK every N (experimental) : (min=0, max=65535, default=0, )
- mss [ number ]
Description: Maximum Segment Size (MSS) : (min=0, max=9146, )
- shutdown_data [ bool ]
Description: Piggy-back Data on Shutdown FIN :
- tcp_4_way_close [ bool ]
Description: 4-way Close :

Description: Piggy-back Data on 3-way Handshake ACK :

Description: Raw Flags : (min=-1, max=255, default=-1, )

- initial_receive_window [ number ]
Description: Initial Receive Window : (min=1, max=65535, )
- retries [ number ]

- psh_every_segment [ bool ]

testmodel.component.dstPortDist
Description: Destination Port : These parameters control the distribution of source ports for TCP connections. Note that setting these parameters to a constant or narrow range can severely limit the available number of tuples that the test component can use for setting up new connections. In the event that the available tuple space is too limited, the test may not achieve the specified number of connections. If this happens, simply expand the range of source or destination ports that the test can use. Constant specifies that the same port will be used for every flow tuple. Range specifies that the ports will be used sequentually, from min to max. This is a best-effort, since other test parameters might cause ports to be reused or skipped. Random specifies no ordering. Ports will be chosen randomly between min to max. Note: Some application protocols enforce source port allocations that can override this parameter as well, depending on the test component and configuration.
Attributes:
- min [ number ]
Description: Minimum Port Number : (min=0, max=65535, )
- max [ number ]
Description: Maximum Port Number : (min=0, max=65535, )
- type [ enum ]
Description: Port Distribution Type :

testmodel.component.rateDist
Description: Data Rate : These parameters defines the maximum transmit data rate that the test will use. When specifying a rate in megabits / second, the ethernet inter-packet gap is included in the rate value. Therefore, the amount of usable data 'on the wire' will be less than the rate value, depending on frame / packet size. Data Rate Unlimited: defines whether data rate limiting should be enabled or disabled for the test. Choose this option for maximum performance or when a test's data rate is naturally limited by other factors such as session rate. This option can be useful for determining the natural upper-bound for a performance test. Data Rate Scope: defines whether the rate distribution number is treated as a per-interface limit or an aggregate limit on the traffic that this component generates. Because of the asymmetric nature of most application protocols, when per-interface limiting is enabled, client-side bandwidth is likely to be less than server-side bandwidth. This means that the aggregate bandwidth used for some protocols will be less than the sum of the max allowed per interface. If you need a fixed amount of throughput, use the aggregate limit. Data Rate Unit: defines the units, either 'Frames / Second' or 'Megabits / Second' that the Minimum/Maximum data rates (below) represent. Data Rate Type: 'Constant' indicates that all generated traffic will be at the data rate specified by the Minimum data rate field, 'Range' indicates that data rate should start at either the Minimum or Maximum data rate and increase or decrease over the course of the test, 'Random' indicates that data rate should be chosen randomly between Minimum and Maximum data rates, inclusive, changing once every tenth of a second during test execution. Minimum/Maximum data rate: min/max data rate. Values of 1 to 1488095 (1 Gigabit ports), 14880952 (10 Gigabit ports), 59523809 (40 Gigabit ports) or 119047619 (100 Gigabit ports) are supported for 'Frames / Second'. Values of 1 to 1000 (1 Gigabit ports), 10000 (10 Gigabit ports), 40000 (40 Gigabit ports) or 80000 (100 Gigabit ports) are supported for 'Megabits / Second'. Note that other rate-related parameters, such as sessions per second or max simultaneous sessions, can cause a test to send less data than specified by this parameter. When other parameters are a limiting factor, this parameter is used only as an upper bound by the test. To ensure maximum throughput, consider the other test parameters as well.
Attributes:
- min [ number ]
Description: Minimum Data Rate : (min=1, default=1000, )
- unit [ enum ]
Description: Data Rate Unit :
- max [ number ]
Description: Maximum Data Rate : (min=1, default=10000, )
- scope [ enum ]
Description: Data Rate Scope :
- unlimited [ bool ]
Description: Data Rate Unlimited : (default=false, )
- type [ enum ]
Description: Data Rate Type :

testmodel.component.payloadSizeDist
Description: Payload Size Distribution : These parameters define the UDP payload/TCP segment size generated by the test component. Distribution Type: 'Constant' indicates that all generated payloads will be the size in the Minimum field. 'Range' indicates that payload sizes should start at Minimum size and increase up to the Maximum size. 'Random' indicates that payload sizes should be chosen randomly between Minimum and Maximum sizes, inclusive. Minimum/Maximum: min/max size of payload (in bytes). Values from 1 to 9146 bytes are supported. This allows a jumbo packet to accomodate a TCP header with 12 bytes of options at the maximum supported frame size of 9216. This restriction also applies to UDP, though it could technically be larger.

testmodel.component.scrambleOptions
Description: StackScrambler : Maximum number of simultaneous corruptions - Specifies the maximum number of corruptions per packet. It is not guaranteed that the maximum number of corruptions will be reached per packet. Corrupt Ethernet Type - The maximum percentage of packets that will have a randomized Ethernet type (16 bits) set in the Ethernet header. Corrupt IP Version - The maximum percentage of packets that will have a randomized IP version number. The Version field specifies the format of the IP packet header. The first 4-bits of both the IPv4 and IPv6 header specifies the version. Corrupt IPv4 Header Length - The maximum percentage of packets that will have a randomized length set. This value is 4 bits in length and specifies the number of 32-bit words in the header. Corrupt IP TTL - The maximum percentage of packets that will have a randomized TTL set. This value is 8 bits in length and specifies the number of hops to traverse before being discarded. In the IPv4 header, this value is known as TTL. In the IPv6 Header, this value is known as Hop Limit. Corrupt IP Differentiated Services - The maximum percentage of packets that will have randomized differentiated services field set in the header. In the IPv4 header, this value was formerly known as TOS (Type of Service). In the IPv6 header, this values is referred to as Traffic Class. In both cases, it is an 8-bit field with the upper 6 bits representing Differentiated Services and the lower 2 bits representing ECN (Explicit Congestion Notification). Corrupt IP Total Length - The maximum percentage of packets that will have a randomized IP total length set in the IP header. In the IPv4 header, this value is 16 bits in length and represents the entire datagram size including the header and data in bytes. In the IPv6 header, this value is 16 bits in length and represents the size of the payload in octets, including any extension headers. Corrupt IPv4 Flags - The maximum percentage of packets that will have randomized IP flags set in the IP header. This value is 3 bits in length and is used to control or identify fragments. Corrupt IPv4 Fragment Offset - The maximum percentage of packets that will have a randomized IP fragment offset set in the IP header. This value is 13 bits in length and specifies the offset of a particular fragment relative to the beginning of the original unfragmented IP datagram. Corrupt IP Protocol - The maximum percentage of packets that will have a bad IP protocol set in the IP header. This value is 8 bits in length and is labeled Protocol in the IPv4 header and Next Header in the IPv6 header. Corrupt IPv4 Checksum - The maximum percentage of packets that will have a randomized IPv4 checksum set in the IP header. This value is 16 bits in length and is used for error-checking of the header. Corrupt IPv4 Options - The maximum percentage of packets transmitted that will have randomized IP options set in the IP header. IP Options are variable in length. Corrupt IPv6 Flow label - The maximum percentage of packets transmitted that will have a randomized Flow label. This value is 20 bits in length and was created for giving real-time applications special service. Corrupt TCP Flags - The maximum percentage of packets transmitted that will have randomized TCP flags set in the TCP header. This value is 8 bits in length and is used to determine the state of the TCP connection. Corrupt TCP Options - The maximum percentage of packets transmitted that will have randomized TCP options set in the TCP header. TCP Options are variable in length. Corrupt TCP or UDP Header Length - The maximum percentage of packets transmitted that will have a randomized TCP or UDP header Length set in the header. In the TCP Header, this value, sometimes called TCP Data Offset, is 4 bits in length and specifies the size of the TCP header in 32-bit words. In the UDP Header, this value is 16 bits in length and specifiec the length of the UDP header and the data. Corrupt TCP Urgent Pointer - The maximum percentage of packets that will have a randomized value urgent pointer set in the TCP header. if the TCP URG flag is set, this 16 bit value is used as an offset from the sequence number indicating the last urgent data byte. Corrupt L4 Checksum - The maximum percentage of packets transmitted that will have a randomized L4 checksum. This value is 16 bits in length and is used for error-checking of the TCP, UDP, or ICMP header and data. Corrupt ICMP Type - The maximum percentage of packets transmitted that will have a randomized ICMP or ICMPv6 Type. This value is 8 bits in length and specifies the type of ICMP message. Corrupt ICMP Code - The maximum percentage of packets transmitted that will have a randomized ICMP or ICMPv6 Code. This value is 8 bits in length and is used for further specification of the ICMP Type. Corrupt SCTP Verification Tag - The maximum percentage of packets transmitted that will have a randomized SCTP Verification Tag. This value is 32 bits in length. Corrupt SCTP Checksum - The maximum percentage of packets transmitted that will have a randomized SCTP Checksum. This value is 32 bits in length. Corrupt SCTP Chunk Type - The maximum percentage of packets transmitted that will have a randomized SCTP Chunk Type. This value is 8 bits in length. Corrupt SCTP Chunk Length - The maximum percentage of packets transmitted that will have a randomized SCTP Chunk Length. This value is 32 bits in length. GTP Corruptions Require a GTP Enabled Network Neighborhood Corrupt GTP-U Flags - The maximum percentage of packets transmitted that will have randomized GTP-U Flags. This value is 8 bits in length. Corrupt GTP-U Type - The maximum percentage of packets transmitted that will have randomized a GTP-U Type. This value is 8 bits in length. Corrupt GTP-U Length - The maximum percentage of packets transmitted that will have randomized a GTP-U Length. This value is 16 bits in length. Corrupt GTP-U Sequence Number - The maximum percentage of packets transmitted that will have randomized a GTP-U Sequence Number. This value is 16 bits in length. Corrupt GTP-U Sequence N-PDU - The maximum percentage of packets transmitted that will have randomized a GTP-U N-PDU. This value is 8 bits in length. Corrupt GTP-U Sequence Next - The maximum percentage of packets transmitted that will have randomized a GTP-U Next. This value is 8 bits in length. Establish TCP Sessions - Whether to send valid handshake packets to establish TCP sessions before starting fuzzing.

testmodel.component@type:layer4
Description: Session Sender: This component measures a device's ability to handle concurrent TCP sessions. It creates and maintains valid TCP sessions with contrived data.
Attributes:
- delayStart [ string ]
Description: Delay Start: Establishes the amount of time before a test component begins. (min=00:00:00, default=00:00:00, )
- packetsPerSession [ number ]
Description: Payload Packets Per Session : This parameter defines how many data packets are to be sent per session. A value of '-1' will cause the test to send an unlimited amount of data instead. The size distribution parameters are applied only to the first 1000 packets in the stream and then repeated. Note that, due to the dynamic nature of TCP, you may see the same data packet sent more than once in a session if the device under test drops a packet and the test must retry the send. (min=-1, max=10000, )

testmodel.component.sessions
Description: Session/Super Flow Configuration : Maximum Super Flows Per Second: This parameter defines the maximum number of Super Flows that will be instantiated per second. If there is one flow per Super Flow, as in Session Sender, this is functionally equivalent to the sum of TCP and UDP flows per second. In cases where there are multiple flows per Super Flow, you may see a varying number of effective flows per second. While there is a limit of 1,000,000 sessions per second per component, be sure to consider several factors when setting this parameter. First, there must be adequate bandwidth allocated to the test via the Rate Distribution parameter to achieve a particular number of sessions per second. For instance, a new TCP session requires approximately 150 bytes to establish when originating out a particular interface. Second, the ramp up duration generally should be 1 second or longer for higher numbers of sessions per second. This ensures that the test has some phase where test bandwidth is exclusively dedicated to setting up sessions. Maximum Simultaneous Active Flows This parameter defines the maximum number of flows that can be active at a time. Active flows includes all flows other than the TCP flows that are currently aging (in the TIME_WAIT state). A value of 0 disables this limit. Maximum Simultaneous Super Flows: This parameter defines the maximum simultaneous Super Flows that will exist concurrently during the test duration. If there is one flow per Super Flow, as in Session Sender, this is functionally equivalent to the sum of TCP and UDP flows. In cases where there are multiple flows per Super Flow, you may see a varying number of effective simultaneous flows. This value defines a shared resource between different test components, and is limited to 60,000,000. In other words, the total maximum simultaneous sessions for all components in a test must be less than or equal to 60,000,000. Unlimited Super Flow Open Rate: This parameter determines globally how fast sessions are opened. If set to true, sessions will be opened as fast as possible. This setting is useful for tests where the session rate is not the limiting factor for a test's performance. Note: this setting may produce session open rates faster than the global limit. Unlimited Super Flow Close Rate: This parameter determines how fast sessions are closed. If set to false, session close rate will mirror the session open rate. If set to true, sessions will be closed as fast as possible. Target Minimum Super Flows Per Second: This parameter specifies a minimum number of sessions that the test must open in order to pass in the final results. This is an aid for the user to define pass/fail criteria for a particular test. This parameter does not affect the network traffic of the test in any way. Target Minimum Simultaneous Super Flows: This parameter specifies a minimum number of sessions per second that the test must open in order to pass in the final results. This is an aid for the user to define pass/fail criteria for a particular test. This parameter does not affect the network traffic of the test in any way. Target Number of Successful matches: This parameter specifies the minimum number of successful matches required to pass in the final results. This is an aid for the user to define pass/fail criteria for a particular test. This parameter does not affect the network traffic of the test in any way. Engine Selection: This parameter selects the type of engine with which to run the test component. Select "Advanced" to enable the default, full-featured engine. Select "Simple" to enable a simpler, higher-performance, stateless engine. Performance Emphasis: This parameter adjusts whether the advanced engine's flow scheduler favors opening new sessions, sending on existing sessions, or a mixture of both. Select "Throughput" to emphasize sending data on existing sessions. Select "Simultaneous Sessions" to emphazise opening new sessions. Select "Balanced" to emphasize both equally - this is the default setting. Note:Ramp-up phases automatically emphasize Sessions, ramp-down phases emphasize Throughput. Resource Allocation Override: This parameter allows the user to override the amount of CPU and other resources allocated to this test component. Normally, the system estimates the amount of resources required by a particular component based on various heuristics. Sometimes, manual tuning is required for optimal performance. The value indicates the amount of resouces to use on a single processor. This parameter is best used when all components are configured for Auto or all components have an override value specified. If the sum of all resources of all components is less than 100%, then this value is treated as a weight, and any extra resources are distributed evenly according to the weight value. Statistic Detail: This parameter adjusts the level of statistics to be collected. Decreasing the number of statistics collected can increase performance and allow for targeted reporting. Select "Maximum" to enable all possible statistics Select "Application Only" to enable only Application statistics (L7) Select "Transport Only" to enable only Transport statistics (L4/L3) Select "Minimum" to disable most statistics
Attributes:
- max [ number ]
Description: Maximum Simultaneous Super Flows : (min=1, )
- closeFast [ bool ]
Description: Unlimited Super Flow Close Rate : (default=false, )
- engine [ enum ]
Description: Engine Selection:
- statDetail [ enum ]
Description: Statistic Detail:
- targetPerSecond [ number ]
Description: Target Minimum Super Flows Per Second : (min=0, max=1000000, )
- openFast [ bool ]
Description: Unlimited Super Flow Open Rate : (default=false, )
- targetMatches [ number ]
Description: Target Number of Successful Matches : (min=0, default=0, )
- maxActive [ number ]
Description: Maximum Simultaneous Active Flows : (min=0, default=0, )
- allocationOverride [ enum ]
Description: Resource Allocation Override : (default=auto, )

testmodel.component.srcPortDist
Description: Source Port : These parameters control the distribution of source ports for TCP connections. Note that setting these parameters to a constant or narrow range can severely limit the available number of tuples that the test component can use for setting up new connections. In the event that the available tuple space is too limited, the test may not achieve the specified number of connections. If this happens, simply expand the range of source or destination ports that the test can use. Constant specifies that the same port will be used for every flow tuple. Range specifies that the ports will be used sequentually, from min to max. This is a best-effort, since other test parameters might cause ports to be reused or skipped. Random specifies no ordering. Ports will be chosen randomly between min to max. Note: Some application protocols enforce source port allocations that can override this parameter as well, depending on the test component and configuration.
Attributes:
- min [ number ]
Description: Minimum Port Number : (min=0, max=65535, )
- max [ number ]
Description: Maximum Port Number : (min=0, max=65535, )
- type [ enum ]
Description: Port Distribution Type :

testmodel.component.rampUpProfile
Description: Ramp Up Profile : Specify how the connection rate should be controlled during the ramp up phase Ramp Up Profile Type: Specifies whether the connection establishment rate should be * Calculated: a constant rate, calculated as the maximum number of sessions divided by ramp up time. This is the default behavior and attempts to reach the overall maximum number of connections over the course of the entire ramp up time. The other parameters are disabled in this mode. This affects ramp-down as well when 'Calculated' mode is specified. * Exact: the configured session rate is honored during the ramp-up phase * Stair Step: a stair-step ramp-up profile defined by user parameters. This also disables the 'Calculated' mode for ramp-down Minimum Connection Rate: Specifies the connection establishment rate to be used at the start of the ramp up phase when not in Calculated mode. Maximum Connection Rate: Limits the maxium connection establishment rate for the ramp up phase when not in Calculated mode. Increment N Connections Per Second: Increases connection establishment rate by this value at every interval when not in Calculated mode. Fixed Time Interval: The interval at which connection establishment rate will be changed when not in Calculated mode.
Attributes:

Description: Min Connection Rate : (min=1, max=4000000, )
- increment [ number ]
Description: Increment n Connections per Interval : (min=1, max=500000, )
- max [ number ]
Description: Max Connection Rate : (min=1, max=4000000, )
- interval [ string ]
Description: Fixed Time Interval : (min=00:00:01, max=300:00:00, default=00:00:01, )
