testmodel.component.payload
Description: Payload : This parameter defines the contents of the data portion of each packet in the test. Where this data is inserted depends on the test type. For TCP, this parameter defines the contents of a TCP segment or segments, depending on other test parameters. For ICMP, this is the data portion of the ICMP echo packet. For UDP and UDP LOSSY, this is the UDP payload. The UDP LOSSY payload type is identical to the UDP payload type except that it does not consider unreceived UDP packets a failure. When the Payload type is specified as '0', data has all bits cleared. When the Payload type is specified as '1', data has all bits set. When the Payload type is specified as 'Random', data is filled with random values. When the Payload type is specified as 'HTTP', data is a simple HTTP request for the '/' URI. If the number of segments is greater than 1, a Content-Length header is added to the request and the request data is padded to fit the size distribution. Otherwise, the request is sent without any added data, regardless of the specified payload size. Warning: combining a GET request with Content-Length or a POST request without a Content-Length field is out of spec and may cause undefined behavior on the remote host. When the Payload type is specified as 'User Defined', data is input in standard hexdecimal notation. If the user specifies less data in the Data field than the specified frame or packet size, this data is repeated in the payload. When Add Payload Timestamp is selected, UDP and ICMP packets are time stamped but all other protocols remain unaffected. Default behavior is to not insert the time stamps.
Attributes:
- add_timestamp [ bool ]
Description: Add Payload Timestamp : (default=false, )
- transport [ enum ]
Description: Transport :
- data [ object ]
Description: User Defined Data :
- http_type [ enum ]
Description: HTTP Request Type :
- type [ enum ]
Description: Type :

testmodel.component.rampDist
Description: Session Ramp Distribution : The session ramp distribution defines 3 distinct phases within a test. The ramp up phase defines a duration where only new TCP sessions are established, but not closed. Other traffic (UDP/ARP/ICMP) is unaffected during this time. This phase is useful to setup a large number of TCP sessions in a short period of time. During the ramp steady-state phase, the test will maintain up to the maximum number of sessions specified open simultaneously. Sessions will open, close and send data as well. During the ramp down phase, any sessions that are open will attempt to close. Ramp Up Behavior: During the ramp up phase, TCP sessions are only opened, but no data is sent. This is useful for quickly setting up a large number of sessions without wasting bandwidth. This parameter defines what the test actually does during the ramp up phase. Note: after the ramp up phase, all sessions will fully open, even if the ramp up behavior was set to something other than "Full Open". "Full Open" - The full TCP handshake is performed on open "Full Open + Data" - Same as full, but start sending data "Full Open + Data + Full Close" - Same as full + data, but also do a full close for completed sessions. "Full Open + Data + Close with Reset" - Same as full + data, but also initiate the TCP close with a RST. "Half Open" - Same as full, but omit the final ACK "SYN Only" - Only SYN packets are sent "Data Only" - Only PSH data packets are sent, with no TCP state machine processing. This mode is not compatible with SSL nor with Conditional Requests. Any flow using SSL will send no packets. SYN Only Retry Mode: Defines the behavior of the TCP Retry Mechanism when dealing with the initial SYN packet of a flow, the following modes are permitted: "Continous" - Continue sending SYN packets, even if we have ran out of retries (Retry Count). "Continous with new session" - Same as "Continous", except we change the initial sequence number every "Retry Count" loop(s). "Obey Retry" - Send no more than "Retry Count" initial SYN packets. NOTE: This option is only active during the ramp up phase and only if the "Ramp Up Behavior" is set to "SYN Only"! Steady-State Behavior: This parameter defines the test behavior during the steady-state phase. This setting is useful for examining connection tracking and timeout behavior of a device under test, as well as maintaining a steady load with a sustained number of simultaneous sessions. "Open and Close Sessions" - sessions are closed as they finish sending data and new ones opened in their place. "Open and Close with Reset" - initiate the TCP close with a RST This bypasses the TCP close state machine. "Open and Close with Reset Response" - respond to a FIN with a RST This bypasses the TCP TIME_WAIT state. "Hold Sessions Open" - sessions are not closed as they finish sending data Ramp Down Behavior: During the Ramp Down phase, no new sessions will be established. As existing sessions complete during the Ramp Down phase, they will be closed in the manner specified by this setting. If a session does not complete before the Ramp Down time has expired, it will remain open. "Full Close" - The full TCP session close is performed "Half Close" - Same as above, but omit the final ACK "Reset" - initiate the TCP close with a RST This bypasses the TCP close state machine. "Reset Response" - respond to a FIN with a RST This bypasses the TCP TIME_WAIT state. #lt;pre#gt; c o s __________maxSessions__________ n e /| |\ c s / | | \ u s / | | \ r i / | | \ r o / | | \ e n / | | \ n s /______|_____________________________|______\ t ramp up ramp steady-state time ramp down time time #lt;/pre#gt;
Attributes:
- downBehavior [ enum ]
Description: Ramp Down Behavior : (default=full, )
- up [ string ]
Description: Ramp Up Duration : (min=0, max=300:00:00, default=00:00:01, )
- upBehavior [ enum ]
Description: Ramp Up Behavior : (default=full, )
- synRetryMode [ enum ]
Description: SYN Only Retry Mode : (default=continuous, )
- down [ string ]
Description: Ramp Down Time Interval : (min=0, max=300:00:00, default=00:00:01, )
- steadyBehavior [ enum ]
Description: Steady-State Behavior : (default=cycle, )
- steady [ string ]
Description: Steady-State Time Interval : (min=0, max=300:00:00, default=00:00:30, )

Values of 0 through 255 (decimal) are supported. Type of Service (TOS)/Differentiated Services Code Point(DSCP): Configures the 8-bit combined TOS/DSCP (also sometimes called DS) field used for all IP packets. testmodel.component.loadprofile
Description: Load Profile : Load Profiles provide you with granular control over the attributes of the ramp-up, steady-state, and ramp down phases that occur during the test. For each phase, you can set the data rate, session rate, session behavior, and the maximum number of simultaneous sessions. If a Load Profile is enabled for the test, then you will not need to configure the following parameters from the Parameters tab: Data Rate Distribution.Data Rate Scope Data Rate Distribution.Data Rate Unit Data Rate Distribution.Data Rate Type Data Rate Distribution.Minimum Data Rate Data Rate Distribution.Maximum Data Rate Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Up Behavior Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Up Seconds Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Steady-State Behavior Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Steady-State Seconds Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Down Behavior Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Down Seconds Session Configuration.Maximum Simultaneous Sessions Session Configuration.Maximum Sessions Per Second The test will retrieve these parameter configurations from the Load Profile. Some Load Profiles will require that you have a specific preset selected for the test. If these Load Profiles do not use the required preset, then the test may not yield the expected stair case behavior. Please note that you must select the preset for the test before you select the Load Profile. To select a preset, go to the Test Editor screen; click the Presets tab; select the appropriate preset; and click the Apply Changes button. Once you have done this, you can go to the Parameters tab and choose the Load Profile. As it is, the BreakingPoint Maximum Sessions Per Second Load Profile will not provide the expected staircase behavior for the test. To simulate staircase behavior, you will need to use the Maximum Possible preset, and you will need to change the values for the following parameters on the Parameters tab: - Payload Size Distribution.Distribution Type must be constant. - Payload Size Distribution.Minimum Size must be 1. - Payload.Type must be 1. - Payload Packets Per Session must be 1.
Attributes:
- name [ string ]
- label [ string ]

testmodel.component.tcp
Description: TCP Configuration : Maximum Segment Size (MSS): The maximum segment size that is advertised during session setup. A value of '0' will automatically configure an optimal MSS for the chosen network, MTU and transport settings. Aging Time: The time, expressed in seconds, that an actively-closed TCP connection will remain in the flow table in the TIME_WAIT state after closing. Flows in the TIME_WAIT count against simultaneous sessions, but do not generate any traffic. Setting this to a high value can cause traffic to slow over time. This setting is useful for matching the flow tracking policy of the DUT. Reset at End: Indicates whether a test should reset all existing TCP connections at the end. If enabled, all TCP connections will reset if the test either ends naturally or is cancelled. Note, RST packets received via this option will not be counted as received at the application layer in reports, only at the TCP and IP layers. Retry Count: Defines the number of retries before a connection is considered errored-out and is canceled by the TCP stack. Retry Quantum: Defines the minimum number of milliseconds between retrying a send. As the number of retries increases, this quantum is doubled for each retry. Delay ACKs: Determines whether to delay ACKing of TCP segments. If enabled, segments are ACKed on the next send, rather than separately on receive. Delayed ACKs ms: Define the minimum number of miliseconds before sending ACK for received segments. Must not exceed the Retry Quantum in order to avoid useless retransmits. A value of "0" will enable a dynamic mechanism that adjusts the value based on the receive window and the retry quantum. Disable Piggy-back Data on ACK (experimental): Forces the transmitting side to send an empty ACK (no data) before starting to send data packets (instead of piggy-backing data on the ACK packets). ACK every N (experimental): This value will force sending an ACK at least every N TCP segments. Default value is 0, which lets the conventional Delay ACKs mechanism work as usual. Note: Forcibly changing the ACK sending pattern is not RFC compliant and can result in unexpected behavior. The TCP protocol itself limits the flexibility of the 'ACK every N' mechanism. In some scenarios we must send an ACK no matter what; this implies that we might send some ACKs earlier that some would expect if the receiver's window fills, the flow ends or the TCP burst ends. In order to improve the pattern's consistency, the recommendation is to set the value for "ACK every N" as a divisor of "TCP Segment Credit" value. Initial Receive Window: Determines the size of the initial receive window for a new connection, in bytes. Internally, the receive window is managed as a number segments of MSS size, so the actual value used is truncated to an MSS multiple. The internal minimum initial value is 1 * MSS. TCP Window Scale: This value will allow the tcp connection to negotiate the window scale option as per RFC1323. The value set can be from 0-14 with 0 being disabled. The value set will be the maximum window size that the connection will attempt to negotiate. The window scale factor is the number of bits by which to shift the window size. Send and receive windows are negotiated separately based on the configuration of the equipment at each end. Dynamic Receive Window Size Determines if the size of the receive window should be increased during test run. The receive window size is increased until it reaches the maximum value (65535 * 2 ^ window_scale_factor). If delayed ACK is enabled, the receive window size is doubled on window full (the remaining receive window size is smaller than MSS), otherwise the receive window size is increased by MSS with each received segment. Add Segment Timestamps: In order to measure inter-packet latency, the stack can add a TCP timestamp option. This expands the size of the TCP header by 12 bytes to 32 bytes, and decreases the effective MSS by 12 bytes. No frame latencies are recorded by the component if this is disabled. Piggy-back Data on 3-way Handshake: Determines whether to add Data to the client ACK packet of the TCP handshake. Piggy-back Data on Shutdown: Determines whether to add Data to the client FIN packet of the TCP shutdown. Initial Congestion Window: Determines the size of the initial congestion window. A value of '0' means the TCP slow start is disabled (the congestion window is not used). Raw Flags: Allows the user to force TCP flags to a particular value, as a decimal number. Add values together to get a combination of TCP flags. Examples: 1 = FIN 2 = SYN 4 = RST 8 = PSH 16 = ACK 32 = URG 64 = ECE 128 = CWR 18 = SYN|ACK -1 Disables this feature (Default). Note: this feature breaks the TCP state machine. Connect Delay: Defines the minimum number of milliseconds between the TCP SYN and SYN|ACK and between the SYN|ACK and the final ACK in the 3-way SYN exchange. The TCP connect delay will end up being twice this number. TCP Keepalive Timer: Number of milliseconds until we send a TCP Keep Alive packet. If a TCP connection is in a "delayed" state, we will send a keep alive ACK every N seconds (N being the value you indicate in this field), zero disables this feature. A connection would be considered "delayed" in one of two ways, either by a SuperFlow stopping on an actual "Client: Delay" or "Server: Delay" action, or if a TCP connection is being held open by selecting the option "Hold Sessions Open" in a "Steady-State" ramp frame. Be advised, the first keep alive packet will be sent at a different interval. If you take this value, divide in half, then add the "TCP Retry Count" from above, that will be the number of milliseconds we will wait until sending the first keep alive packet. For example, if you set this value to 10000 ms and the Retry Counter to 2000 ms, the first keep alive will be sent 7000 ms from being "delayed" (10000/2 + 2000 = 7000) and then every 10000 milliseconds until the end of the flow or it is closed. 4-way Close: When a FIN packet is received, this option simulates the TCP half-close ability. Please be aware that no data can be sent/received after the connection is closed. Send PSH with all data segments: If enabled, every data segment will have the PSH flag on. Otherwise, the behaviour will stay default. SYN data padding size: This field only works on the SYN-ONLY mode, that enables TCP SYN Flood functionality. With "SYN data padding size" we can select the payload size of the data attached to the SYN packets in the SYN-ONLY mode.
Attributes:
- syn_data_padding [ number ]
Description: SYN data padding size: (min=0, max=1440, default=0, )
- delay_acks [ bool ]
Description: Delay ACKs :
- retry_quantum_ms [ number ]
Description: Retry Quantum : (min=1, max=2000, )
- tcp_connect_delay_ms [ number ]
Description: Connect Delay : (min=0, max=10, default=0, )
- reset_at_end [ bool ]
Description: Reset at End :
- disable_ack_piggyback [ bool ]
Description: Disable Piggy-back data on ACK (experimental) :
- tcp_icw [ number ]
Description: Initial Congestion Window : (min=0, max=16, default=0, )
- aging_time_data_type [ enum ]
Description: Aging Time Data Type: (default=aging_time_data_type_sc, )
- delay_acks_ms [ number ]
Description: Delayed ACKs ms : (min=0, max=500, default=0, )
- aging_time [ number ]
Description: Aging Time : (min=0, max=120, )
- tcp_window_scale [ number ]
Description: TCP Window Scale : (min=0, max=14, )
- dynamic_receive_window_size [ bool ]
Description: Dynamic Receive Window Size : (default=true, )
- add_timestamps [ bool ]
Description: Add Segment Timestamps :
- ack_every_n [ number ]
Description: ACK every N (experimental) : (min=0, max=65535, default=0, )
- mss [ number ]
Description: Maximum Segment Size (MSS) : (min=0, max=9146, )
- shutdown_data [ bool ]
Description: Piggy-back Data on Shutdown FIN :
- tcp_4_way_close [ bool ]
Description: 4-way Close :
- handshake_data [ bool ]
Description: Piggy-back Data on 3-way Handshake ACK :
- raw_flags [ number ]
Description: Raw Flags : (min=-1, max=255, default=-1, )
- tcp_keepalive_timer [ number ]
Description: TCP Keepalive Timer: (min=0, max=4294967295, default=0, )
- initial_receive_window [ number ]
Description: Initial Receive Window : (min=1, max=65535, )

testmodel.component.rateDist
Description: Data Rate : These parameters defines the maximum transmit data rate that the test will use. When specifying a rate in megabits / second, the ethernet inter-packet gap is included in the rate value. Therefore, the amount of usable data 'on the wire' will be less than the rate value, depending on frame / packet size. Data Rate Unlimited: defines whether data rate limiting should be enabled or disabled for the test. Choose this option for maximum performance or when a test's data rate is naturally limited by other factors such as session rate. This option can be useful for determining the natural upper-bound for a performance test. Data Rate Scope: defines whether the rate distribution number is treated as a per-interface limit or an aggregate limit on the traffic that this component generates. Because of the asymmetric nature of most application protocols, when per-interface limiting is enabled, client-side bandwidth is likely to be less than server-side bandwidth. This means that the aggregate bandwidth used for some protocols will be less than the sum of the max allowed per interface. If you need a fixed amount of throughput, use the aggregate limit. Data Rate Unit: defines the units, either 'Frames / Second' or 'Megabits / Second' that the Minimum/Maximum data rates (below) represent. Data Rate Type: 'Constant' indicates that all generated traffic will be at the data rate specified by the Minimum data rate field, 'Range' indicates that data rate should start at either the Minimum or Maximum data rate and increase or decrease over the course of the test, 'Random' indicates that data rate should be chosen randomly between Minimum and Maximum data rates, inclusive, changing once every tenth of a second during test execution. Minimum/Maximum data rate: min/max data rate. Values of 1 to 1488095 (1 Gigabit ports), 14880952 (10 Gigabit ports), 59523809 (40 Gigabit ports) or 119047619 (100 Gigabit ports) are supported for 'Frames / Second'. Values of 1 to 1000 (1 Gigabit ports), 10000 (10 Gigabit ports), 40000 (40 Gigabit ports) or 80000 (100 Gigabit ports) are supported for 'Megabits / Second'. Note that other rate-related parameters, such as sessions per second or max simultaneous sessions, can cause a test to send less data than specified by this parameter. When other parameters are a limiting factor, this parameter is used only as an upper bound by the test. To ensure maximum throughput, consider the other test parameters as well.
Attributes:
- min [ number ]
Description: Minimum Data Rate : (min=1, default=1000, )
- unit [ enum ]
Description: Data Rate Unit :
- max [ number ]
Description: Maximum Data Rate : (min=1, default=10000, )
- scope [ enum ]
Description: Data Rate Scope :
- unlimited [ bool ]
Description: Data Rate Unlimited : (default=false, )
- type [ enum ]
Description: Data Rate Type :

'Range' indicates that payload sizes should start at Minimum size and increase up to the Maximum size. 'Random' indicates that payload sizes should be chosen randomly between Minimum and Maximum sizes, inclusive. Minimum/Maximum: min/max size of payload (in bytes). Values from 1 to 9146 bytes are supported. This allows a jumbo packet to accomodate a TCP header with 12 bytes of options at the maximum supported frame size of 9216. This restriction also applies to UDP, though it could technically be larger.

Description: Advanced Options - Enable TCP: This parameter specifies that a TCP packet will be generated. If enabled, the system will send pre-defined TCP packets instead of UDP packets during the test. The user may override the contents of the TCP packet, up to byte 128, using the specifying 'User Defined' payload type. Data specified will overwrite the packet contents starting after the port numbers in the TCP header (offset 4 into the TCP header.) The portion of user-specified data falling within the TCP checksum area will be ignored. Note: This parameter is being deprecated, please use the packet template parameter to enable TCP packets. The slow start traffic is sent at rate of approximately 100 to 500 packets/second. This traffic is usually sent in the reverse direction to advertise the MAC addresses of the target devices to the DUT.

testmodel.component.payload
Description: Payload : This parameter defines the contents of the data portion of each packet in the test. Where this data is inserted depends on the test type. For Bit Blaster, this parameter defines the payload after the Ethernet header. For Routing Robot, this is the UDP payload. For Session Sender, this parameter defines the contents of a TCP segment. When the Payload type is specified as '0', data has all bits cleared. When the Payload type is specified as '1', data has all bits set. When the Payload type is specified as 'Random', data is filled with random values. When the Payload type is specified as 'Increment', data is filled with ascending values based on the data width setting. When the Payload type is specified as 'Decrement', data is filled with descending values based on the data width setting. When the Payload type is specified as 'User Defined', data is input in standard hexdecimal notation. If the user specifies less data in the Data field than the specified frame or packet size, this data is repeated in the payload. Data Width: when Payload type is 'Increment' or 'Decrement', this value indicates the width (in bits) of the data values being manipulated.
Attributes:
- dataWidth [ enum ]
Description: Data Width : (default=eight, )
- data [ object ]
Description: User Defined Data :
- type [ enum ]
Description: Type :

testmodel.component.advancedIPv4
Description: Advanced Options - IPv4: Time To Live (TTL): The maximum bound on the number-of-hops that an IP datagram can exist in an internet system before it is dropped. Values of 0 through 255 (decimal) are supported. Type of Service (TOS): Configures the TOS field used for all IP packets. This field is sometimes used to implement quality of service features. Early TOS IP implementations have been deprecated, and have been superceded by the DiffServ model. Values of 0 through FF (hexadecimal) are supported, please note that TOS and DiffServ are bit field encodings. Length Field: 'Actual' indicates the correct IP datagram length should be populated in the IP header 'total length' field, 'Constant' indicates the Length value should be placed in the IP header 'total length' field. Length Value: when IP length field is set to 'Constant', this indicates the value to be placed in the IP header 'total length' field. Values of 0 through 65535 (decimal) are supported. Checksum Field: 'Actual' indicates the correct IP header checksum should be populated in the IP header 'checksum' field, 'Constant' indicates the Checksum value should be placed in the IP header 'checksum' field. Checksum Value: when IP length field is set to 'Constant', this indicates the value to be placed in the IP header 'checksum' field. Values of 0 through FFFF (hexadecimal) are supported. Option Header Field: if 'enabled', allows up to 40 bytes of IP option data to be specified. If 'disabled', the UDP header will directly follow the IPv4 header. Option Header Data: if Option Header Field is 'enabled', this field provides IPv4 option data. Data is input in standard hexdecimal notation, with a limit of 40 bytes.

testmodel.component.sizeDist
Description: Size Distribution: These parameters define the frame/packet size(s) generated by the test component. Size Distribution Unit: 'Frame' indicates the 14 byte Ethernet header and 4 byte Ethernet frame CRC is included in the specifed size, 'Packet' indicates the Ethernet header/CRC is not included in the specified size. Size Distribution Type: 'Constant' indicates that all generated frames/packets will be the size in the Minimum Frame/Packet Size field, 'Mix' indicates up to 10 different frame/packet sizes will be used with a weighting factor per size, 'Random' indicates that frame/packet sizes should be chosen randomly between Minimum and Maximum Frame/Packet Size's, inclusive, changing once every second during test execution, 'Range' indicates that frame/packet sizes should start at Minimum Frame/Packet Size field and increase up to the Maximum Frame/Packet Size. Minimum/Maximum Frame/Packet Size: min/max size of frames/packets (in bytes). Values of 64 to 9216 are supported for frames. Values of 46 to 9198 are supported for packets. Please review for the Overheads section below for more information about minimum frame/packet sizes. Increment N Bytes: when Size Distribution Type is 'Range', this value indicates the "step" amount (in bytes) to incrementally change the size during the course of the test. When this value is positive, the test will begin with frames/packets that are the Minimum Frame/Packet Size in size. Values of -128 to 128 are supported. Every N Seconds: when Size Distribution Type is 'Range', this value indicates the delay (in seconds) between frame/packet size changes. Values of 1 to 3600 are supported. Overheads: The Bit Blaster and Routing Robot components use the last 16 bytes (before the Ethernet CRC) of the packet/frame for hardware signature verification. The overheads of VLAN tags, IPv4 or IPv6 headers (including option fields and extension headers) and upper layer templates (such as UDP/TCP headers) all reserve space that must be factored into the minimum packet/frame size required. The 16 byte signature field is used in all configurations and an error warning will result if not enough space is reserved for the hardware signature in the packet/frame as defined by the test parameters and Network Neighborhood.
Attributes:
- type [ enum ]
Description: Size Distribution Type :
- mixlen9 [ number ]

- mixlen10 [ number ]
Description: Length of Mix Distribution 10 : (min=0, max=9216, default=0, )

Description: Every N Seconds : (min=1, max=3600, default=1, )

Description: Weight of Mix Distribution 2 : (min=0, max=10000, default=0, )

Description: Minimum Frame/Packet Size : (min=46, max=9216, default=64, )
- increment [ number ]
Description: Increment N Bytes : (min=-128, max=128, default=0, )
- mixweight8 [ number ]

testmodel.component.Templates
Description: Packet Templates: The templates parameter provides alternative packet definitions to the standard UDP packet that is used by the Routing Robot component. They provide a quick method to generate rate based traffic with several different packet types. Template Types: UDP: use the default behavior of Routing Robot TCP: a generic TCP packet template (ACK only flag set) TCP Syn Flood: a TCP syn packet template (syn only flag set) ICMP Echo Request: ICMP Echo Reply: When a template type of TCP is selected, this parameter supersedes the deprecated "enableTCP" option.

testmodel.component.payloadAdvanced
Description: Advanced Options - Payload : These parameters allow placement of a User Defined Field (UDF) into the payload data. The UDF can either be an incrementing counter or byte pattern, which overwrites the existing payload data so the packet length is unchanged. Where this data is placed depends on the test type. In this test component, the payload begins after the UDP header. UDF mode: 'Counter' will insert a 1-to-4 byte (UDF length) counter which increments every frame, 'Random' will insert a 1-to-end-of-payload (UDF length) sequence of random values, 'Increment'/'Decrement' will insert a 1-to-end-of-payload (UDF length) sequence of incrementing/decrementing values, using a 8, 16, or 32-bit width specified by UDF data width. 'Disabled' will not use the UDF in the test. UDF offset: indicates the number of bytes from the beginning of the payload to place the UDF data. Values of 0 to 9173 are supported, with 0 being the first byte of the payload. UDF length: indicates the UDF length (in bytes). Values of 1 to 9174 are supported. UDF data width: when UDF mode is 'Increment' or 'Decrement', this value indicates the width (in bits) of the data values being manipulated. Payload Note: Packets generated by this test component will reserve the last 16 bytes of the payload for internal use by BreakingPoint Systems. These bytes will not contain the payload value that you have defined, if any.
Attributes:
- udfDataWidth [ enum ]
Description: UDF data width : (default=eight, )
- udfOffset [ number ]
Description: UDF offset : (min=0, max=9173, )
- udfMode [ enum ]
Description: UDF mode :
- udfLength [ number ]
Description: UDF length : (min=1, max=9174, )

testmodel.component.rateDist
Description: Data Rate: These parameters define the maximum transmit data rate that the test will use per-interface. When specifying a rate in megabits / second, the ethernet inter-packet gap is included in the rate value. Therefore, the amount of usable data 'on the wire' will be less than the rate value, depending on frame / packet size. Data Rate Unit: defines the units, either 'Frames / Second' or 'Megabits / Second' that the Minimum/Maximum data rates (below) represent. Data Rate Type: 'Constant' indicates that all generated traffic will be at the data rate specified by the Minimum data rate field, 'Range' indicates that data rate should start at either the Minimum or Maximum data rate and increase or decrease over the course of the test (see Increment field below), 'Random' indicates that data rate should be chosen randomly between Minimum and Maximum data rates, inclusive, changing once every second during test execution. Minimum/Maximum data rate: min/max data rate. Values of 1 to 1488095 (1 Gigabit ports), 14880952 (10 Gigabit ports), 59523809 (40 Gigabit ports) or 119047619 (100 Gigabit ports) are supported for 'Frames / Second'. Values of 1 to 1000 (1 Gigabit ports), 10000 (10 Gigabit ports), 40000 (40 Gigabit ports) or 80000 (100 Gigabit ports) are supported for 'Megabits / Second'. * Increment N units: when Data Rate Type is 'Range', this value indicates the "step" amount (in frames / second or Megabits / Second, based on the data rate unit value) to incrementally change the rate during the course of the test. When this value is positive, the test will begin at the Minimum data rate as its rate. When this value is negative, the test will begin with the Maximum data rate as its rate. Values of -10000 to 10000 are supported. Ramp Type: When Data Rate Type is 'Range', this value indicates what to do when reaching the maximum or minimum range value. The setting, 'wrap' will reset the data rate to the initial rate value at the start of the test and 'limit' will hold the terminating data rate till the end of the test. Every N Seconds: when Data Rate Type is 'Range', this value indicates the delay (in seconds) between rate changes. Values of 1 to 3600 are supported. *: Actual transmit rate may vary by up to 2% from configured value, due to 5 nanosecond granularity within the interpacket timer. The effect will be most pronounced at packet sizes of 100 bytes or less.
Attributes:
- min [ number ]
Description: Minimum Data Rate : (min=1, default=1000, )
- increment [ number ]
Description: Increment N Units/Period : (min=-10000, max=10000, default=0, )
- unit [ enum ]
Description: Data Rate Unit :
- rate [ number ]
Description: Every N Seconds : (min=1, max=3600, default=1, )
- max [ number ]
Description: Maximum Data Rate : (min=1, default=1000, )
- ramptype [ enum ]
Description: Data Rate Ramp : (default=wrap, )
- type [ enum ]
Description: Data Rate Type :

Length Value: when UDP length field is set to 'Constant', this indicates the value to be placed in the UDP header 'length' field. Values of 0 through 65535 (decimal) are supported. Checksum Field: 'Actual' indicates the correct UDP checksum should be populated in the UDP header 'checksum' field, 'Constant' indicates the Checksum value should be placed in the UDP header 'checksum' field. Checksum Value: when UDP length field is set to 'Constant', this indicates the value to be placed in the UDP header 'checksum' field. Values of 0 through FFFF (hexadecimal) are supported.

testmodel.component@type:layer3
Description: Routing Robot: This component measures a device's ability to accurately route IP packets. It sends IP packets with contrived payloads, and measures whether the packets reach their intended destination.
Attributes:
- dstPortMask [ number ]
Description: Destination Port Mask Length: Destination port mask length. This mask length value sets how many of the rightmost bits in the port field can be modified for each packet. Values of 16 (all bits) to 1 are supported. (min=1, max=16, default=16, )
- srcPort [ number ]
Description: Source Port: UDP port that packets indicate they are addressed from. Values of 0 through 65535 (decimal) are supported. (min=0, max=65535, default=1, )
- maxStreams [ number ]
Description: Maximum Stream Count: This override parameter sets the maximum number of streams to use for this component. It allows the user to reduce the unique stream count to a subset of the total streams possible with the network neighborhood configuration. Note that with the Routing Robot component, users are already able to limit the number of streams by specifying minimum and maximum IP address range values. The Maximum Stream Count sets the number of rightmost bits which change in a address (MAC and/or IP). For switched networks, the patterns of all 1's is not used in the varied bit fields. For routed networks, the all 1's pattern, the all 0's pattern, and the router gateway addresses are not used. An example: in a routed network neighborhood that has a network mask of 8, we would like to limit the # of streams to 32 or less. Set the Max Stream Count in the component to 32. This indicates that the 5 most right bits can change (2**5 == 32), and since the neighborhood is routed, there will be 29 unique streams generated. If a non-power of 2 value is specified in Maximum Stream Count, the value used will be lowered down value of the next power of 2. For example if 31 is specified, the value implied will be 16 indicating that the 4 bits of rightmost addresses will be allowed to change. This component requires that the 3 rightmost bits in the address are modifiable. Therefore the minimum value of this parameter is 8. (min=8, max=16777216, default=64, )
- syncIP [ bool ]
Description: Synchronize IP Ranges: Setting this parameter will limit or synchronize the range of the source and destination IP addresses to the smaller of the two. The default behavior of Routing Robot is to use the maximum and minimum ranges set in the Network Neighborhood. If the ranges are not of an equivalent size, a larger number of streams are used, so with this option enabled the ranges will be adjusted so that IP addresses will be in sync. If either the source or destination IP range is 0, this is a fixed address and no adjustments are made. (default=false, )
- bidirectional [ bool ]
Description: Bidirectional: Originate traffic from both the client and server interfaces. (default=false, )
- udpDstPortMode [ enum ]
Description: Destination Port Modifier: Selects modification type of the destination port field.
- addrGenMode [ enum ]
Description: IP Address Algorithm: Determines the IP address modification type. The Performance option will use Random mode if possible, but use Increment mode for data rates and frame sizes that requires the setting to meet timing requirements.
- slowStartFps [ number ]
Description: Slow Start Rate: This parameter sets the rate of the slow start traffic. The rate is specified in the number of frames per second. A setting of zero indicates that the component will auto-calculate the rate so that the slow start phase will complete in approximately 5 seconds. (min=0, max=1000000, default=32, )
- enableTCP [ bool ]
Description: Advanced Options - Enable TCP: This parameter specifies that a TCP packet will be generated. If enabled, the system will send pre-defined TCP packets instead of UDP packets during the test. The user may override the contents of the TCP packet, up to byte 128, using the specifying 'User Defined' payload type. Data specified will overwrite the packet contents starting after the port numbers in the TCP header (offset 4 into the TCP header.) The portion of user-specified data falling within the TCP checksum area will be ignored. Note: This parameter is being deprecated, please use the packet template parameter to enable TCP packets. If a packet template other than the default UDP is specified, this parameter will be ignored. (default=false, )
- dstPort [ number ]
Description: Destination Port: UDP port that packets indicate they are addressed to. Values of 0 through 65535 (decimal) are supported. (min=0, max=65535, default=1, )
- slowStart [ bool ]
Description: Slow Start: This parameter specifies if the test component is allowed to send a small amount of traffic at the beginning of the test before ramping up to the full rate of the test. This will allow routing DUTs to warm their ARP cache and switching DUTs to identify which port to send test-generated traffic. The slow start traffic is sent at rate of approximately 100 to 500 packets/second. This traffic is usually sent in the reverse direction to advertise the MAC addresses of the target devices to the DUT.
- udpSrcPortMode [ enum ]
Description: Source Port Modifier: Selects modification type of the source port field.
- randomizeIP [ bool ]
Description: Randomize IP Start Address: Setting this parameter will configure the initial IP source and destination addresses to a random value within the specified Network Neighborhood range. If this parameter is not set, the minimum value in the range is used for the initial addresses. (default=false, )
- delayStart [ string ]
Description: Delay Start: Establishes the amount of time before a test component begins. (min=00:00:00, default=00:00:00, )
- srcPortMask [ number ]
Description: Source Port Mask Length: Source port mask length. This mask length value sets how many of the rightmost bits in the port field can be modified for each packet. Values of 16 (all bits) to 1 are supported. (min=1, max=16, default=16, )

testmodel.component.advancedIPv6
Description: Advanced Options - IPv6: Hop Limit: The maximum bound on the number-of-hops that an IP datagram can exist in an internet system before it is dropped. Values of 0 through 255 (decimal) are supported. Traffic Class: Configures the Traffic class field used for all IP packets. Values of 0 through FF (hexadecimal) are supported. Flow Label: Configures the Flow label field used for all IP packets. Values of 0 through FFFF (hexadecimal) are supported. Length Field: 'Actual' indicates the correct IP datagram length should be populated in the IP header 'payload length' field, 'Constant' indicates the Length value should be placed in the IP header 'packet length' field. Length Value: when IP length field is set to 'Constant', this indicates the value to be placed in the IP header 'total length' field. Values of 0 through 65535 (decimal) are supported. Extension Header Field: if 'enabled', allows up to 56 bytes of extension header(s) to be specified. If 'disabled', the UDP header will directly follow the IPv6 header. Next Header: if Extension Header Field is 'enabled', this field provides the Next header value to populate in the IPv6 header, describing the type of extension header that appears first in the Extension header data field. Extension Header Data: if Extension Header Field is 'enabled', this field provides IPv6 extension header(s). Data is input in standard hexdecimal notation, with a limit of 56 bytes. It in incumbent on the user to ensure the last extension header's Next header field be a hex value of 11 to indicate a UDP payload.

testmodel.component.payload
Description: Payload : This parameter defines the contents of the data portion of each packet in the test. Where this data is inserted depends on the test type. For Bit Blaster, this parameter defines the payload after the Ethernet header. For Routing Robot, this is the UDP payload. For Session Sender, this parameter defines the contents of a TCP segment. When the Payload type is specified as '0', data has all bits cleared. When the Payload type is specified as '1', data has all bits set. When the Payload type is specified as 'Random', data is filled with random values. When the Payload type is specified as 'Increment', data is filled with ascending values based on the data width setting. When the Payload type is specified as 'Decrement', data is filled with descending values based on the data width setting. When the Payload type is specified as 'User Defined', data is input in standard hexdecimal notation. If the user specifies less data in the Data field than the specified frame or packet size, this data is repeated in the payload. Data Width: when Payload type is 'Increment' or 'Decrement', this value indicates the width (in bits) of the data values being manipulated.
Attributes:

Description: Data Width : (default=eight, )

testmodel.component.payloadAdvanced
Description: Advanced Options - Payload : These parameters allow placement of a User Defined Field (UDF) into the payload data. The UDF can either be an incrementing counter or byte pattern, which overwrites the existing payload data so the packet length is unchanged. Where this data is placed depends on the test type. In this test component, the payload begins after the UDP header. UDF mode: 'Counter' will insert a 1-to-4 byte (UDF length) counter which increments every frame, 'Random' will insert a 1-to-end-of-payload (UDF length) sequence of random values, 'Increment'/'Decrement' will insert a 1-to-end-of-payload (UDF length) sequence of incrementing/decrementing values, using a 8, 16, or 32-bit width specified by UDF data width. 'Disabled' will not use the UDF in the test. UDF offset: indicates the number of bytes from the beginning of the payload to place the UDF data. Values of 0 to 9173 are supported, with 0 being the first byte of the payload. UDF length: indicates the UDF length (in bytes). Values of 1 to 9174 are supported. UDF data width: when UDF mode is 'Increment' or 'Decrement', this value indicates the width (in bits) of the data values being manipulated. Payload Note: Packets generated by this test component will reserve the last 16 bytes of the payload for internal use by BreakingPoint Systems. These bytes will not contain the payload value that you have defined, if any.
Attributes:
- udfDataWidth [ enum ]
Description: UDF data width : (default=eight, )
- udfOffset [ number ]
Description: UDF offset : (min=0, max=9173, )
- udfMode [ enum ]
Description: UDF mode :
- udfLength [ number ]
Description: UDF length : (min=1, max=9174, )

testmodel.component.rateDist
Description: Data Rate: These parameters define the maximum transmit data rate that the test will use per-interface. When specifying a rate in megabits / second, the ethernet inter-packet gap is included in the rate value. Therefore, the amount of usable data 'on the wire' will be less than the rate value, depending on frame / packet size. Data Rate Unit: defines the units, either 'Frames / Second' or 'Megabits / Second' that the Minimum/Maximum data rates (below) represent. Data Rate Type: 'Constant' indicates that all generated traffic will be at the data rate specified by the Minimum data rate field, 'Range' indicates that data rate should start at either the Minimum or Maximum data rate and increase or decrease over the course of the test (see Increment field below), 'Random' indicates that data rate should be chosen randomly between Minimum and Maximum data rates, inclusive, changing once every second during test execution. Minimum/Maximum data rate: min/max data rate. Values of 1 to 1488095 (1 Gigabit ports), 14880952 (10 Gigabit ports), 59523809 (40 Gigabit ports) or 119047619 (100 Gigabit ports) are supported for 'Frames / Second'. Values of 1 to 1000 (1 Gigabit ports), 10000 (10 Gigabit ports), 40000 (40 Gigabit ports) or 80000 (100 Gigabit ports) are supported for 'Megabits / Second'. * Increment N units: when Data Rate Type is 'Range', this value indicates the "step" amount (in frames / second or Megabits / Second, based on the data rate unit value) to incrementally change the rate during the course of the test. When this value is positive, the test will begin at the Minimum data rate as its rate. When this value is negative, the test will begin with the Maximum data rate as its rate. Values of -10000 to 10000 are supported. Ramp Type: When Data Rate Type is 'Range', this value indicates what to do when reaching the maximum or minimum range value. The setting, 'wrap' will reset the data rate to the initial rate value at the start of the test and 'limit' will hold the terminating data rate till the end of the test. Every N Seconds: when Data Rate Type is 'Range', this value indicates the delay (in seconds) between rate changes. Values of 1 to 3600 are supported. *: Actual transmit rate may vary by up to 2% from configured value, due to 5 nanosecond granularity within the interpacket timer. The effect will be most pronounced at packet sizes of 100 bytes or less.
Attributes:
- min [ number ]
Description: Minimum Data Rate : (min=1, default=1000, )
- increment [ number ]
Description: Increment N Units/Period : (min=-10000, max=10000, default=0, )
- unit [ enum ]
Description: Data Rate Unit :
- rate [ number ]
Description: Every N Seconds : (min=1, max=3600, default=1, )
- max [ number ]
Description: Maximum Data Rate : (min=1, default=1000, )
- ramptype [ enum ]
Description: Data Rate Ramp : (default=wrap, )
- type [ enum ]
Description: Data Rate Type :

testmodel.component@type:playback
Description: Recreate: This component recreates captured traffic patterns.
Attributes:
- behavior [ enum ]
Description: General Behavior: General Behavior: When a capture file is imported through Traffic Manager, it is stored in three different ways, allowing the Recreate Component to replay the traffic in three different modes: Mode 1: During capture file import, each complete flow's Layer 4-Layer 7 data is stored in individual files and grouped according to protocol. - The delay between each packet within each flow is recorded. - Periodically, the bandwidth in use is recorded. - Periodically, the total number of currently open sessions is recorded. - Periodically, the "weight", or relationship of currently open flows grouped by protocol is recorded. - The duration of the test is recorded. * These individual files grouped by protocol, are only used whe Replay Capture File Without Modification is set to false. When the Recreate Component is run in this mode, flows are randomly chosen according to protocol weight. The Layer 2, Layer 3, and Layer 4 headers honor Network Neighborhood and Recreate Configuration Parameters such as Session/Super Flow Configuration, IPv4 Configuration, IPv6 Configuration, Source Port, TCP Configuration, and Data Rate. Modification Options are ignored, except for General Behavior. Replay Capture File With Server IP Intact will use the server IP for all the flows during replay from capture file. How the General Behavior Settings are interpretted in this mode: Use User-Specified Settings: - The Data Rate and Session/Super Flow Configuration Parameters are honored. - The duration of the test is controlled by the Load Profile. Use Capture File Settings - Periodically recorded bandwidth in use is honored during the duration of the test. - Periodically recorded total number of currently open sessions is honored. - The duration of the test is set to the duration of the imported capture file. Mode 2: During capture file import, an exact copy of the imported capture file is stored. Use case: This mode is useful for testing Layer 2, Layer 3, and Layer 4 anomalies such as fragmentation, invalid packets, retransmissions, and other protocols not properly converted into Layer 4 - Layer 7 payloads. * This file is only used when Replay Capture File Without Modification is set to true. When the Recreate Component is run in this mode, the test duration defined by the Load Profile is not honored, the test ends when all packets are retransmitted. Network Neighborhood settings are also ignored. All packets are sent from the client interface. Ability to speficy BPF Filter. Ability to specify start and end packet to be transmitted. Ability to specify the Number of Times to Loop Capture File. How the General Behavior Settings are interpretted in this mode: Use User-Specified Settings - The capture file is retransmitted, ignoring the delay between each packet. Use Capture File Settings - The capture file is retransmitted, honoring the delay between each packet. Mode 3: During capture file import, the first 255 flow's Layer 4-Layer 7 data is stored in a single file. Use case: This mode is useful when it is necessary to control the order of the individual flows. - The delay between each packet is recorded. - Periodically, the bandwidth in use is recorded. - Periodically, the total number of currently open sessions is recorded. - The duration of the test is recorded. * This file is only used when Replay Capture File In Single Mode is set to true. - Replay Capture File in Single Mode set to true. The first 255 flows's Layer 4 - Layer 7 data is stored in a single file. - The delay between each packet within each flow is recorded. Replay Capture File With Server IP Intact will use the server IP for all the flows during replay from capture file. Independent Flow Hosts In Single Mode will cause each flow allocate a new server/client IP. This option is necessary to run packet capture which contains both Ipv4 flows and IPv6 flows in Single Mode. How the General Behavior Settings are interpretted in this mode: Identical to Mode 1.
- delayStart [ string ]
Description: Delay Start: Establishes the amount of time before a test component begins. (min=00:00:00, default=00:00:00, )
- file [ object ]
Description: Capture File: Capture File - Sets the capture file that will be used to recreate traffic.

testmodel.component.sessions
Description: Session/Super Flow Configuration : Maximum Super Flows Per Second: This parameter defines the maximum number of Super Flows that will be instantiated per second. If there is one flow per Super Flow, as in Session Sender, this is functionally equivalent to the sum of TCP and UDP flows per second. In cases where there are multiple flows per Super Flow, you may see a varying number of effective flows per second. While there is a limit of 1,000,000 sessions per second per component, be sure to consider several factors when setting this parameter. First, there must be adequate bandwidth allocated to the test via the Rate Distribution parameter to achieve a particular number of sessions per second. For instance, a new TCP session requires approximately 150 bytes to establish when originating out a particular interface. Second, the ramp up duration generally should be 1 second or longer for higher numbers of sessions per second. This ensures that the test has some phase where test bandwidth is exclusively dedicated to setting up sessions. Maximum Simultaneous Active Flows This parameter defines the maximum number of flows that can be active at a time. Active flows includes all flows other than the TCP flows that are currently aging (in the TIME_WAIT state). A value of 0 disables this limit. Maximum Simultaneous Super Flows: This parameter defines the maximum simultaneous Super Flows that will exist concurrently during the test duration. If there is one flow per Super Flow, as in Session Sender, this is functionally equivalent to the sum of TCP and UDP flows. In cases where there are multiple flows per Super Flow, you may see a varying number of effective simultaneous flows. This value defines a shared resource between different test components, and is limited to 60,000,000. In other words, the total maximum simultaneous sessions for all components in a test must be less than or equal to 60,000,000. Unlimited Super Flow Open Rate: This parameter determines globally how fast sessions are opened. If set to true, sessions will be opened as fast as possible. This setting is useful for tests where the session rate is not the limiting factor for a test's performance. Note: this setting may produce session open rates faster than the global limit. Unlimited Super Flow Close Rate: This parameter determines how fast sessions are closed. If set to false, session close rate will mirror the session open rate. If set to true, sessions will be closed as fast as possible. Target Minimum Super Flows Per Second: This parameter specifies a minimum number of sessions that the test must open in order to pass in the final results. This is an aid for the user to define pass/fail criteria for a particular test. This parameter does not affect the network traffic of the test in any way. Target Minimum Simultaneous Super Flows: This parameter specifies a minimum number of sessions per second that the test must open in order to pass in the final results. This is an aid for the user to define pass/fail criteria for a particular test. This parameter does not affect the network traffic of the test in any way. Target Number of Successful matches: This parameter specifies the minimum number of successful matches required to pass in the final results. This is an aid for the user to define pass/fail criteria for a particular test. This parameter does not affect the network traffic of the test in any way. Engine Selection: This parameter selects the type of engine with which to run the test component. Select "Advanced" to enable the default, full-featured engine. Select "Simple" to enable a simpler, higher-performance, stateless engine. Performance Emphasis: This parameter adjusts whether the advanced engine's flow scheduler favors opening new sessions, sending on existing sessions, or a mixture of both. Select "Throughput" to emphasize sending data on existing sessions. Select "Simultaneous Sessions" to emphazise opening new sessions. Select "Balanced" to emphasize both equally - this is the default setting. Note:Ramp-up phases automatically emphasize Sessions, ramp-down phases emphasize Throughput. Resource Allocation Override: This parameter allows the user to override the amount of CPU and other resources allocated to this test component. Normally, the system estimates the amount of resources required by a particular component based on various heuristics. Sometimes, manual tuning is required for optimal performance. The value indicates the amount of resouces to use on a single processor. This parameter is best used when all components are configured for Auto or all components have an override value specified. If the sum of all resources of all components is less than 100%, then this value is treated as a weight, and any extra resources are distributed evenly according to the weight value. Statistic Detail: This parameter adjusts the level of statistics to be collected. Decreasing the number of statistics collected can increase performance and allow for targeted reporting. Select "Maximum" to enable all possible statistics Select "Application Only" to enable only Application statistics (L7) Select "Transport Only" to enable only Transport statistics (L4/L3) Select "Minimum" to disable most statistics
Attributes:
- max [ number ]
Description: Maximum Simultaneous Super Flows : (min=1, )
- closeFast [ bool ]
Description: Unlimited Super Flow Close Rate : (default=false, )
- engine [ enum ]
Description: Engine Selection:
- statDetail [ enum ]
Description: Statistic Detail:
- targetPerSecond [ number ]
Description: Target Minimum Super Flows Per Second : (min=0, max=1000000, )
- openFast [ bool ]
Description: Unlimited Super Flow Open Rate : (default=false, )

testmodel.component.srcPortDist
Description: Source Port: These parameters control the distribution of source ports for TCP connections. Note that setting these parameters to a constant or narrow range can severely limit the available number of tuples that the test component can use for setting up new connections. In the event that the available tuple space is too limited, the test may not achieve the specified number of connections. If this happens, simply expand the range of source or destination ports that the test can use. Constant specifies that the same port will be used for every flow tuple. Range specifies that the ports will be used sequentually, from min to max. This is a best-effort, since other test parameters might cause ports to be reused or skipped. Random specifies no ordering. Ports will be chosen randomly between min to max. Note: Some application protocols enforce source port allocations that can override this parameter as well, depending on the test component and configuration.
Attributes:
- min [ number ]
Description: Minimum Port Number : (min=0, max=65535, )
- max [ number ]
Description: Maximum Port Number : (min=0, max=65535, )
- type [ enum ]
Description: Port Distribution Type :

This is the default behavior and attempts to reach the overall maximum number of connections over the course of the entire ramp up time. The other parameters are disabled in this mode. This affects ramp-down as well when 'Calculated' mode is specified. * Exact: the configured session rate is honored during the ramp-up phase * Stair Step: a stair-step ramp-up profile defined by user parameters. This also disables the 'Calculated' mode for ramp-down Minimum Connection Rate: Specifies the connection establishment rate to be used at the start of the ramp up phase when not in Calculated mode. Maximum Connection Rate: Limits the maxium connection establishment rate for the ramp up phase when not in Calculated mode. Increment N Connections Per Second: Increases connection establishment rate by this value at every interval when not in Calculated mode. Fixed Time Interval: The interval at which connection establishment rate will be changed when not in Calculated mode.

testmodel.component.rampDist
Description: Session Ramp Distribution : The session ramp distribution defines 3 distinct phases within a test. The ramp up phase defines a duration where only new TCP sessions are established, but not closed. Other traffic (UDP/ARP/ICMP) is unaffected during this time. This phase is useful to setup a large number of TCP sessions in a short period of time. During the ramp steady-state phase, the test will maintain up to the maximum number of sessions specified open simultaneously. Sessions will open, close and send data as well. During the ramp down phase, any sessions that are open will attempt to close. Ramp Up Behavior: During the ramp up phase, TCP sessions are only opened, but no data is sent. This is useful for quickly setting up a large number of sessions without wasting bandwidth. This parameter defines what the test actually does during the ramp up phase. Note: after the ramp up phase, all sessions will fully open, even if the ramp up behavior was set to something other than "Full Open". "Full Open" - The full TCP handshake is performed on open "Full Open + Data" - Same as full, but start sending data "Full Open + Data + Full Close" - Same as full + data, but also do a full close for completed sessions. "Full Open + Data + Close with Reset" - Same as full + data, but also initiate the TCP close with a RST. "Half Open" - Same as full, but omit the final ACK "SYN Only" - Only SYN packets are sent "Data Only" - Only PSH data packets are sent, with no TCP state machine processing. This mode is not compatible with SSL nor with Conditional Requests. Any flow using SSL will send no packets. SYN Only Retry Mode: Defines the behavior of the TCP Retry Mechanism when dealing with the initial SYN packet of a flow, the following modes are permitted: "Continous" - Continue sending SYN packets, even if we have ran out of retries (Retry Count). "Continous with new session" - Same as "Continous", except we change the initial sequence number every "Retry Count" loop(s). "Obey Retry" - Send no more than "Retry Count" initial SYN packets. NOTE: This option is only active during the ramp up phase and only if the "Ramp Up Behavior" is set to "SYN Only"! Steady-State Behavior: This parameter defines the test behavior during the steady-state phase. This setting is useful for examining connection tracking and timeout behavior of a device under test, as well as maintaining a steady load with a sustained number of simultaneous sessions. "Open and Close Sessions" - sessions are closed as they finish sending data and new ones opened in their place. "Open and Close with Reset" - initiate the TCP close with a RST This bypasses the TCP close state machine. "Open and Close with Reset Response" - respond to a FIN with a RST This bypasses the TCP TIME_WAIT state. "Hold Sessions Open" - sessions are not closed as they finish sending data Ramp Down Behavior: During the Ramp Down phase, no new sessions will be established. As existing sessions complete during the Ramp Down phase, they will be closed in the manner specified by this setting. If a session does not complete before the Ramp Down time has expired, it will remain open. "Full Close" - The full TCP session close is performed "Half Close" - Same as above, but omit the final ACK "Reset" - initiate the TCP close with a RST This bypasses the TCP close state machine. "Reset Response" - respond to a FIN with a RST This bypasses the TCP TIME_WAIT state. #lt;pre#gt; c o s __________maxSessions__________ n e /| |\ c s / | | \ u s / | | \ r i / | | \ r o / | | \ e n / | | \ n s /______|_____________________________|______\ t ramp up ramp steady-state time ramp down time time #lt;/pre#gt;
Attributes:
- downBehavior [ enum ]
Description: Ramp Down Behavior : (default=full, )
- up [ string ]
Description: Ramp Up Duration : (min=0, max=300:00:00, default=00:00:01, )
- upBehavior [ enum ]
Description: Ramp Up Behavior : (default=full, )
- synRetryMode [ enum ]
Description: SYN Only Retry Mode : (default=continuous, )
- down [ string ]
Description: Ramp Down Time Interval : (min=0, max=300:00:00, default=00:00:01, )
- steadyBehavior [ enum ]
Description: Steady-State Behavior : (default=cycle, )
- steady [ string ]
Description: Steady-State Time Interval : (min=0, max=300:00:00, default=00:00:30, )

testmodel.component.loadprofile
Description: Load Profile : Load Profiles provide you with granular control over the attributes of the ramp-up, steady-state, and ramp down phases that occur during the test. For each phase, you can set the data rate, session rate, session behavior, and the maximum number of simultaneous sessions. If a Load Profile is enabled for the test, then you will not need to configure the following parameters from the Parameters tab: Data Rate Distribution.Data Rate Scope Data Rate Distribution.Data Rate Unit Data Rate Distribution.Data Rate Type Data Rate Distribution.Minimum Data Rate Data Rate Distribution.Maximum Data Rate Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Up Behavior Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Up Seconds Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Steady-State Behavior Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Steady-State Seconds Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Down Behavior Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Down Seconds Session Configuration.Maximum Simultaneous Sessions Session Configuration.Maximum Sessions Per Second The test will retrieve these parameter configurations from the Load Profile. Some Load Profiles will require that you have a specific preset selected for the test. If these Load Profiles do not use the required preset, then the test may not yield the expected stair case behavior. Please note that you must select the preset for the test before you select the Load Profile. To select a preset, go to the Test Editor screen; click the Presets tab; select the appropriate preset; and click the Apply Changes button. Once you have done this, you can go to the Parameters tab and choose the Load Profile. As it is, the BreakingPoint Maximum Sessions Per Second Load Profile will not provide the expected staircase behavior for the test. To simulate staircase behavior, you will need to use the Maximum Possible preset, and you will need to change the values for the following parameters on the Parameters tab: - Payload Size Distribution.Distribution Type must be constant. - Payload Size Distribution.Minimum Size must be 1. - Payload.Type must be 1. - Payload Packets Per Session must be 1.

testmodel.component.modification
Description: Modification Options : These settings modify how precisely the capture file is followed. Replay Capture File Without Modification - This mode replays libpcap formatted capture files without modifying Layer 2 through Layer 7. Recreate will derive all settings and configurations from the PCAP file. There are a few trade-offs when operating in this mode: Recreate will only track the Interface Stats, and the capture file can only be replayed at a maximum of 40 Mbps. Replay Capture File In Single Mode - This mode replays the L4 Payloads of all of the flows (up to 255) of the imported capture file in order. Independent Flow Hosts In Single Mode - Each flow of the imported capture file will have different L3 address. Replay Capture File With Server IP Intact - The server L3 address will be kept intact as in capture file during replay while client IP will be replaced with IP configured in Network Neighbourhood. Rewrite Source and Destination - Rewrite source and destination ports that match Original Port to New Port. This option can only be used when Replay capture file without modification is set to false. A value or 0 for Original Port or New Port disables this feature. Loop Count - Number of times to replay capture file without modification. BPF Filter String - tcpdump style BPF filter string. When set, only matching packets will be played back. This option can only be used when Replay capture file without modification is set to true. Start Packet - Specify the starting packet number for playback. End Packet - Specify the ending packet for playback. If left blank, playback will continue to end of the capture file.

testmodel.component.tcp
Description: TCP Configuration : Maximum Segment Size (MSS): The maximum segment size that is advertised during session setup. A value of '0' will automatically configure an optimal MSS for the chosen network, MTU and transport settings. Aging Time: The time, expressed in seconds, that an actively-closed TCP connection will remain in the flow table in the TIME_WAIT state after closing. Flows in the TIME_WAIT count against simultaneous sessions, but do not generate any traffic. Setting this to a high value can cause traffic to slow over time. This setting is useful for matching the flow tracking policy of the DUT. Reset at End: Indicates whether a test should reset all existing TCP connections at the end. If enabled, all TCP connections will reset if the test either ends naturally or is cancelled. Note, RST packets received via this option will not be counted as received at the application layer in reports, only at the TCP and IP layers. Retry Count: Defines the number of retries before a connection is considered errored-out and is canceled by the TCP stack. Retry Quantum: Defines the minimum number of milliseconds between retrying a send. As the number of retries increases, this quantum is doubled for each retry. Delay ACKs: Determines whether to delay ACKing of TCP segments. If enabled, segments are ACKed on the next send, rather than separately on receive. Delayed ACKs ms: Define the minimum number of miliseconds before sending ACK for received segments. Must not exceed the Retry Quantum in order to avoid useless retransmits. A value of "0" will enable a dynamic mechanism that adjusts the value based on the receive window and the retry quantum. Disable Piggy-back Data on ACK (experimental): Forces the transmitting side to send an empty ACK (no data) before starting to send data packets (instead of piggy-backing data on the ACK packets). ACK every N (experimental): This value will force sending an ACK at least every N TCP segments. Default value is 0, which lets the conventional Delay ACKs mechanism work as usual. Note: Forcibly changing the ACK sending pattern is not RFC compliant and can result in unexpected behavior. The TCP protocol itself limits the flexibility of the 'ACK every N' mechanism. In some scenarios we must send an ACK no matter what; this implies that we might send some ACKs earlier that some would expect if the receiver's window fills, the flow ends or the TCP burst ends. In order to improve the pattern's consistency, the recommendation is to set the value for "ACK every N" as a divisor of "TCP Segment Credit" value. Initial Receive Window: Determines the size of the initial receive window for a new connection, in bytes. Internally, the receive window is managed as a number segments of MSS size, so the actual value used is truncated to an MSS multiple. The internal minimum initial value is 1 * MSS. TCP Window Scale: This value will allow the tcp connection to negotiate the window scale option as per RFC1323. The value set can be from 0-14 with 0 being disabled. The value set will be the maximum window size that the connection will attempt to negotiate. The window scale factor is the number of bits by which to shift the window size. Send and receive windows are negotiated separately based on the configuration of the equipment at each end. Dynamic Receive Window Size Determines if the size of the receive window should be increased during test run. The receive window size is increased until it reaches the maximum value (65535 * 2 ^ window_scale_factor). If delayed ACK is enabled, the receive window size is doubled on window full (the remaining receive window size is smaller than MSS), otherwise the receive window size is increased by MSS with each received segment. Add Segment Timestamps: In order to measure inter-packet latency, the stack can add a TCP timestamp option. This expands the size of the TCP header by 12 bytes to 32 bytes, and decreases the effective MSS by 12 bytes. No frame latencies are recorded by the component if this is disabled. Piggy-back Data on 3-way Handshake: Determines whether to add Data to the client ACK packet of the TCP handshake. Piggy-back Data on Shutdown: Determines whether to add Data to the client FIN packet of the TCP shutdown. Initial Congestion Window: Determines the size of the initial congestion window. A value of '0' means the TCP slow start is disabled (the congestion window is not used). Raw Flags: Allows the user to force TCP flags to a particular value, as a decimal number. Add values together to get a combination of TCP flags. Examples: 1 = FIN 2 = SYN 4 = RST 8 = PSH 16 = ACK 32 = URG 64 = ECE 128 = CWR 18 = SYN|ACK -1 Disables this feature (Default). Note: this feature breaks the TCP state machine. Connect Delay: Defines the minimum number of milliseconds between the TCP SYN and SYN|ACK and between the SYN|ACK and the final ACK in the 3-way SYN exchange. The TCP connect delay will end up being twice this number. TCP Keepalive Timer: Number of milliseconds until we send a TCP Keep Alive packet. If a TCP connection is in a "delayed" state, we will send a keep alive ACK every N seconds (N being the value you indicate in this field), zero disables this feature. A connection would be considered "delayed" in one of two ways, either by a SuperFlow stopping on an actual "Client: Delay" or "Server: Delay" action, or if a TCP connection is being held open by selecting the option "Hold Sessions Open" in a "Steady-State" ramp frame. Be advised, the first keep alive packet will be sent at a different interval. If you take this value, divide in half, then add the "TCP Retry Count" from above, that will be the number of milliseconds we will wait until sending the first keep alive packet. For example, if you set this value to 10000 ms and the Retry Counter to 2000 ms, the first keep alive will be sent 7000 ms from being "delayed" (10000/2 + 2000 = 7000) and then every 10000 milliseconds until the end of the flow or it is closed. 4-way Close: When a FIN packet is received, this option simulates the TCP half-close ability. Please be aware that no data can be sent/received after the connection is closed. Send PSH with all data segments: If enabled, every data segment will have the PSH flag on. Otherwise, the behaviour will stay default. SYN data padding size: This field only works on the SYN-ONLY mode, that enables TCP SYN Flood functionality. With "SYN data padding size" we can select the payload size of the data attached to the SYN packets in the SYN-ONLY mode.
Attributes:
- syn_data_padding [ number ]
Description: SYN data padding size: (min=0, max=1440, default=0, )
- delay_acks [ bool ]
Description: Delay ACKs :
- retry_quantum_ms [ number ]
Description: Retry Quantum : (min=1, max=2000, )
- tcp_connect_delay_ms [ number ]
Description: Connect Delay : (min=0, max=10, default=0, )
- reset_at_end [ bool ]
Description: Reset at End :
- disable_ack_piggyback [ bool ]
Description: Disable Piggy-back data on ACK (experimental) :
- tcp_icw [ number ]
Description: Initial Congestion Window : (min=0, max=16, default=0, )
- aging_time_data_type [ enum ]

- delay_acks_ms [ number ]
Description: Delayed ACKs ms : (min=0, max=500, default=0, )

testmodel.component.rateDist
Description: Data Rate: These parameters defines the maximum transmit data rate that the test will use. When specifying a rate in megabits / second, the ethernet inter-packet gap is included in the rate value. Therefore, the amount of usable data 'on the wire' will be less than the rate value, depending on frame / packet size. Data Rate Unlimited: defines whether data rate limiting should be enabled or disabled for the test. Choose this option for maximum performance or when a test's data rate is naturally limited by other factors such as session rate. This option can be useful for determining the natural upper-bound for a performance test. Data Rate Scope: defines whether the rate distribution number is treated as a per-interface limit or an aggregate limit on the traffic that this component generates. Because of the asymmetric nature of most application protocols, when per-interface limiting is enabled, client-side bandwidth is likely to be less than server-side bandwidth. This means that the aggregate bandwidth used for some protocols will be less than the sum of the max allowed per interface. If you need a fixed amount of throughput, use the aggregate limit. Data Rate Unit: defines the units, either 'Frames / Second' or 'Megabits / Second' that the Minimum/Maximum data rates (below) represent. Data Rate Type: 'Constant' indicates that all generated traffic will be at the data rate specified by the Minimum data rate field, 'Range' indicates that data rate should start at either the Minimum or Maximum data rate and increase or decrease over the course of the test, 'Random' indicates that data rate should be chosen randomly between Minimum and Maximum data rates, inclusive, changing once every tenth of a second during test execution. Minimum/Maximum data rate: min/max data rate. Values of 1 to 1488095 (1 Gigabit ports), 14880952 (10 Gigabit ports), 59523809 (40 Gigabit ports) or 119047619 (100 Gigabit ports) are supported for 'Frames / Second'. Values of 1 to 1000 (1 Gigabit ports), 10000 (10 Gigabit ports), 40000 (40 Gigabit ports) or 80000 (100 Gigabit ports) are supported for 'Megabits / Second'. Note that other rate-related parameters, such as sessions per second or max simultaneous sessions, can cause a test to send less data than specified by this parameter. When other parameters are a limiting factor, this parameter is used only as an upper bound by the test. To ensure maximum throughput, consider the other test parameters as well.
Attributes:
- min [ number ]
Description: Minimum Data Rate : (min=1, default=1000, )
- unit [ enum ]
Description: Data Rate Unit :
- max [ number ]
Description: Maximum Data Rate : (min=1, default=10000, )
- scope [ enum ]
Description: Data Rate Scope :
- unlimited [ bool ]
Description: Data Rate Unlimited : (default=false, )
- type [ enum ]
Description: Data Rate Type :

- attackPlan [ string ]

- attackProfile [ string ]
Description: Evasion Profile : The name of the evasion profile for this test. An evasion profile provides a set of default parameters that override those in the strike list.
- attackPlanIterations [ number ]
