testmodel.component.rampDist
Description: Session Ramp Distribution : The session ramp distribution defines 3 distinct phases within a test. The ramp up phase defines a duration where only new TCP sessions are established, but not closed. Other traffic (UDP/ARP/ICMP) is unaffected during this time. This phase is useful to setup a large number of TCP sessions in a short period of time. During the ramp steady-state phase, the test will maintain up to the maximum number of sessions specified open simultaneously. Sessions will open, close and send data as well. During the ramp down phase, any sessions that are open will attempt to close. Ramp Up Behavior: During the ramp up phase, TCP sessions are only opened, but no data is sent. This is useful for quickly setting up a large number of sessions without wasting bandwidth. This parameter defines what the test actually does during the ramp up phase. Note: after the ramp up phase, all sessions will fully open, even if the ramp up behavior was set to something other than "Full Open". "Full Open" - The full TCP handshake is performed on open "Full Open + Data" - Same as full, but start sending data "Full Open + Data + Full Close" - Same as full + data, but also do a full close for completed sessions. "Full Open + Data + Close with Reset" - Same as full + data, but also initiate the TCP close with a RST. "Half Open" - Same as full, but omit the final ACK "SYN Only" - Only SYN packets are sent "Data Only" - Only PSH data packets are sent, with no TCP state machine processing. This mode is not compatible with SSL nor with Conditional Requests. Any flow using SSL will send no packets. SYN Only Retry Mode: Defines the behavior of the TCP Retry Mechanism when dealing with the initial SYN packet of a flow, the following modes are permitted: "Continous" - Continue sending SYN packets, even if we have ran out of retries (Retry Count). "Continous with new session" - Same as "Continous", except we change the initial sequence number every "Retry Count" loop(s). "Obey Retry" - Send no more than "Retry Count" initial SYN packets. NOTE: This option is only active during the ramp up phase and only if the "Ramp Up Behavior" is set to "SYN Only"! Steady-State Behavior: This parameter defines the test behavior during the steady-state phase. This setting is useful for examining connection tracking and timeout behavior of a device under test, as well as maintaining a steady load with a sustained number of simultaneous sessions. "Open and Close Sessions" - sessions are closed as they finish sending data and new ones opened in their place. "Open and Close with Reset" - initiate the TCP close with a RST This bypasses the TCP close state machine. "Open and Close with Reset Response" - respond to a FIN with a RST This bypasses the TCP TIME_WAIT state. "Hold Sessions Open" - sessions are not closed as they finish sending data Ramp Down Behavior: During the Ramp Down phase, no new sessions will be established. As existing sessions complete during the Ramp Down phase, they will be closed in the manner specified by this setting. If a session does not complete before the Ramp Down time has expired, it will remain open. "Full Close" - The full TCP session close is performed "Half Close" - Same as above, but omit the final ACK "Reset" - initiate the TCP close with a RST This bypasses the TCP close state machine. "Reset Response" - respond to a FIN with a RST This bypasses the TCP TIME_WAIT state. #lt;pre#gt; c o s __________maxSessions__________ n e /| |\ c s / | | \ u s / | | \ r i / | | \ r o / | | \ e n / | | \ n s /______|_____________________________|______\ t ramp up ramp steady-state time ramp down time time #lt;/pre#gt;
Attributes:
- downBehavior [ enum ]
Description: Ramp Down Behavior : (default=full, )
- up [ string ]
Description: Ramp Up Duration : (min=0, max=300:00:00, default=00:00:01, )
- upBehavior [ enum ]
Description: Ramp Up Behavior : (default=full, )
- synRetryMode [ enum ]
Description: SYN Only Retry Mode : (default=continuous, )
- down [ string ]
Description: Ramp Down Time Interval : (min=0, max=300:00:00, default=00:00:01, )
- steadyBehavior [ enum ]
Description: Steady-State Behavior : (default=cycle, )
- steady [ string ]
Description: Steady-State Time Interval : (min=0, max=300:00:00, default=00:00:30, )

testmodel.component.loadprofile
Description: Load Profile : Load Profiles provide you with granular control over the attributes of the ramp-up, steady-state, and ramp down phases that occur during the test. For each phase, you can set the data rate, session rate, session behavior, and the maximum number of simultaneous sessions. If a Load Profile is enabled for the test, then you will not need to configure the following parameters from the Parameters tab: Data Rate Distribution.Data Rate Scope Data Rate Distribution.Data Rate Unit Data Rate Distribution.Data Rate Type Data Rate Distribution.Minimum Data Rate Data Rate Distribution.Maximum Data Rate Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Up Behavior Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Up Seconds Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Steady-State Behavior Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Steady-State Seconds Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Down Behavior Session Ramp Distribution.Ramp Down Seconds Session Configuration.Maximum Simultaneous Sessions Session Configuration.Maximum Sessions Per Second The test will retrieve these parameter configurations from the Load Profile. Some Load Profiles will require that you have a specific preset selected for the test. If these Load Profiles do not use the required preset, then the test may not yield the expected stair case behavior. Please note that you must select the preset for the test before you select the Load Profile. To select a preset, go to the Test Editor screen; click the Presets tab; select the appropriate preset; and click the Apply Changes button. Once you have done this, you can go to the Parameters tab and choose the Load Profile. As it is, the BreakingPoint Maximum Sessions Per Second Load Profile will not provide the expected staircase behavior for the test. To simulate staircase behavior, you will need to use the Maximum Possible preset, and you will need to change the values for the following parameters on the Parameters tab: - Payload Size Distribution.Distribution Type must be constant. - Payload Size Distribution.Minimum Size must be 1. - Payload.Type must be 1. - Payload Packets Per Session must be 1.
Attributes:
- name [ string ]
- label [ string ]

testmodel.component.tcp
Description: TCP Configuration : Maximum Segment Size (MSS): The maximum segment size that is advertised during session setup. A value of '0' will automatically configure an optimal MSS for the chosen network, MTU and transport settings. Aging Time: The time, expressed in seconds, that an actively-closed TCP connection will remain in the flow table in the TIME_WAIT state after closing. Flows in the TIME_WAIT count against simultaneous sessions, but do not generate any traffic. Setting this to a high value can cause traffic to slow over time. This setting is useful for matching the flow tracking policy of the DUT. Reset at End: Indicates whether a test should reset all existing TCP connections at the end. If enabled, all TCP connections will reset if the test either ends naturally or is cancelled. Note, RST packets received via this option will not be counted as received at the application layer in reports, only at the TCP and IP layers. Retry Count: Defines the number of retries before a connection is considered errored-out and is canceled by the TCP stack. Retry Quantum: Defines the minimum number of milliseconds between retrying a send. As the number of retries increases, this quantum is doubled for each retry. Delay ACKs: Determines whether to delay ACKing of TCP segments. If enabled, segments are ACKed on the next send, rather than separately on receive. Delayed ACKs ms: Define the minimum number of miliseconds before sending ACK for received segments. Must not exceed the Retry Quantum in order to avoid useless retransmits. A value of "0" will enable a dynamic mechanism that adjusts the value based on the receive window and the retry quantum. Disable Piggy-back Data on ACK (experimental): Forces the transmitting side to send an empty ACK (no data) before starting to send data packets (instead of piggy-backing data on the ACK packets). ACK every N (experimental): This value will force sending an ACK at least every N TCP segments. Default value is 0, which lets the conventional Delay ACKs mechanism work as usual. Note: Forcibly changing the ACK sending pattern is not RFC compliant and can result in unexpected behavior. The TCP protocol itself limits the flexibility of the 'ACK every N' mechanism. In some scenarios we must send an ACK no matter what; this implies that we might send some ACKs earlier that some would expect if the receiver's window fills, the flow ends or the TCP burst ends. In order to improve the pattern's consistency, the recommendation is to set the value for "ACK every N" as a divisor of "TCP Segment Credit" value. Initial Receive Window: Determines the size of the initial receive window for a new connection, in bytes. Internally, the receive window is managed as a number segments of MSS size, so the actual value used is truncated to an MSS multiple. The internal minimum initial value is 1 * MSS. TCP Window Scale: This value will allow the tcp connection to negotiate the window scale option as per RFC1323. The value set can be from 0-14 with 0 being disabled. The value set will be the maximum window size that the connection will attempt to negotiate. The window scale factor is the number of bits by which to shift the window size. Send and receive windows are negotiated separately based on the configuration of the equipment at each end. Dynamic Receive Window Size Determines if the size of the receive window should be increased during test run. The receive window size is increased until it reaches the maximum value (65535 * 2 ^ window_scale_factor). If delayed ACK is enabled, the receive window size is doubled on window full (the remaining receive window size is smaller than MSS), otherwise the receive window size is increased by MSS with each received segment. Add Segment Timestamps: In order to measure inter-packet latency, the stack can add a TCP timestamp option. This expands the size of the TCP header by 12 bytes to 32 bytes, and decreases the effective MSS by 12 bytes. No frame latencies are recorded by the component if this is disabled. Piggy-back Data on 3-way Handshake: Determines whether to add Data to the client ACK packet of the TCP handshake. Piggy-back Data on Shutdown: Determines whether to add Data to the client FIN packet of the TCP shutdown. Initial Congestion Window: Determines the size of the initial congestion window. A value of '0' means the TCP slow start is disabled (the congestion window is not used). Raw Flags: Allows the user to force TCP flags to a particular value, as a decimal number. Add values together to get a combination of TCP flags. Examples: 1 = FIN 2 = SYN 4 = RST 8 = PSH 16 = ACK 32 = URG 64 = ECE 128 = CWR 18 = SYN|ACK -1 Disables this feature (Default). Note: this feature breaks the TCP state machine. Connect Delay: Defines the minimum number of milliseconds between the TCP SYN and SYN|ACK and between the SYN|ACK and the final ACK in the 3-way SYN exchange. The TCP connect delay will end up being twice this number. TCP Keepalive Timer: Number of milliseconds until we send a TCP Keep Alive packet. If a TCP connection is in a "delayed" state, we will send a keep alive ACK every N seconds (N being the value you indicate in this field), zero disables this feature. A connection would be considered "delayed" in one of two ways, either by a SuperFlow stopping on an actual "Client: Delay" or "Server: Delay" action, or if a TCP connection is being held open by selecting the option "Hold Sessions Open" in a "Steady-State" ramp frame. Be advised, the first keep alive packet will be sent at a different interval. If you take this value, divide in half, then add the "TCP Retry Count" from above, that will be the number of milliseconds we will wait until sending the first keep alive packet. For example, if you set this value to 10000 ms and the Retry Counter to 2000 ms, the first keep alive will be sent 7000 ms from being "delayed" (10000/2 + 2000 = 7000) and then every 10000 milliseconds until the end of the flow or it is closed. 4-way Close: When a FIN packet is received, this option simulates the TCP half-close ability. Please be aware that no data can be sent/received after the connection is closed. Send PSH with all data segments: If enabled, every data segment will have the PSH flag on. Otherwise, the behaviour will stay default. SYN data padding size: This field only works on the SYN-ONLY mode, that enables TCP SYN Flood functionality. With "SYN data padding size" we can select the payload size of the data attached to the SYN packets in the SYN-ONLY mode.
Attributes:
- syn_data_padding [ number ]
Description: SYN data padding size: (min=0, max=1440, default=0, )
- delay_acks [ bool ]
Description: Delay ACKs :
- retry_quantum_ms [ number ]
Description: Retry Quantum : (min=1, max=2000, )
- tcp_connect_delay_ms [ number ]
Description: Connect Delay : (min=0, max=10, default=0, )
- reset_at_end [ bool ]
Description: Reset at End :
- disable_ack_piggyback [ bool ]
Description: Disable Piggy-back data on ACK (experimental) :

Description: Aging Time Data Type: (default=aging_time_data_type_sc, )
- delay_acks_ms [ number ]

testmodel.component.rateDist
Description: Data Rate : This parameter defines the maximum transmit data rate that the test will use. When specifying a rate in megabits / second, the ethernet inter-packet gap is included in the rate value. Therefore, the amount of usable data 'on the wire' will be less than the rate value, depending on frame / packet size. Data Rate Automactic: defines whether data rate limiting should be only enabled per Superflow basis for the test as opposed to some global limit across all Superflows. Choose this option to follow the average bandwidth calculated from Live Profile and limiting bandwidth for each Superflow associated in a phase acoording to that. Data Rate Scope: defines whether the rate distribution number is treated as a per-interface limit or an aggregate limit on the traffic that this component generates. Because of the asymmetric nature of most application protocols, when per-interface limiting is enabled, client-side bandwidth is likely to be less than server-side bandwidth. This means that the aggregate bandwidth used for some protocols will be less than the sum of the max allowed per interface. If you need a fixed amount of throughput, use the aggregate limit. Data Rate Unit: defines the units, either 'Frames / Second' or 'Megabits / Second' that the Minimum/Maximum data rates (below) represent. Data Rate Type: 'Constant' indicates that all generated traffic will be at the data rate specified by the Minimum data rate field, 'Range' indicates that data rate should start at either the Minimum or Maximum data rate and increase or decrease over the course of the test, 'Random' indicates that data rate should be chosen randomly between Minimum and Maximum data rates, inclusive, changing once every tenth of a second during test execution. Minimum/Maximum data rate: min/max data rate. Values of 1 to 1488095 (1 Gigabit ports), 14880952 (10 Gigabit ports), 59523809 (40 Gigabit ports) or 119047619 (100 Gigabit ports) are supported for 'Frames / Second'. Values of 1 to 1000 (1 Gigabit ports), 10000 (10 Gigabit ports), 40000 (40 Gigabit ports) or 80000 (100 Gigabit ports) are supported for 'Megabits / Second'. Note that other rate-related parameters, such as sessions per second or max simultaneous sessions, can cause a test to send less data than specified by this parameter. These session parameters are internally calculated for each phase for each of the superflows.
Attributes:
- min [ number ]
Description: Minimum Data Rate : (min=1, )
- unit [ enum ]
Description: Data Rate Unit :
- max [ number ]
Description: Maximum Data Rate : (min=1, )
- scope [ enum ]
Description: Data Rate Scope :
- unlimited [ bool ]
Description: Data Rate Automatic : (default=false, )
- type [ enum ]
Description: Data Rate Type :

(runid) = Test RUN ID
(reportType) = Report file format to be exported in.
(sectionIds) = Chapter Ids. Can be extracted a chapter or many, a sub-chapter or many or the entire report: (sectionIds='6' / sectionIds='5,6,7' / sectionIds='7.4,8.5.2,8.6.3.1' / sectionIds=''(to export the entire report))
(dataType) = Report content data type to export. Default value is 'all data'. For tabular only use 'TABLE' and for graphs only use 'CHARTS'.

network.networkModel.interface.impairments
Description: Impairments: Corruptions applied to outbound packets
Attributes:
- corrupt_rand [ bool ]
Description: Randomly Corrupt Packet: Corrupts packets in a random location within the packet byte of the packet (default=false, )
- corrupt_lt64 [ bool ]
Description: Corrupt Packet in Bytes 1-64: Corrupts packets only within the first 64 bytes of the packet (default=false, )
- rate [ object ]
Description: Corruption Rate: Percentage of packets corrupted (min=0, max=100, default=10, )
- frack [ bool ]
Description: Frack Packet: Separates the packet into 8-byte portions and randomly removes portions from the packet (default=false, )
- drop [ bool ]
Description: Drop Packet: Drops packets (default=false, )
- corrupt_chksum [ bool ]
Description: Corrupt IP Checksum: Creates an invalid checksum (default=false, )
- corrupt_lt256 [ bool ]

- corrupt_gt256 [ bool ]
Description: Corrupt Packet in Bytes 257-end: Corrupts packets after the first 256 bytes (default=false, )

Description: IKE Integrity: IKE integrity algorithm (default=AUTH_HMAC_SHA1_96, )

network.networkModel.ds_lite_b4
No Description.
Attributes:
- prefix_length [ number ]
Description: B4 Prefix Length: Defines the prefix length of the B4 IPv6 address (in bits) (min=8, max=127, default=64, )
- host_ip_addr_alloc_mode [ enum ]
Description: Host IPv4 address allocation mode : Static: the starting IPv4 host address will be the one set in the 'IPv4 STATIC HOSTS' element range which has as container this DS-LITE B4 range. The address will be configured in the static host range in the 'Base IP Address' field. The address count will be also the one set in the 'IPv4 STATIC HOSTS' element range as well as the Netmask. Static/CPE defined: the starting IPv4 host address will be the one set in the 'Host IPv4 Base Address', but the count will be the one set in the 'IPv4 STATIC HOSTS' element range which has as container this DS-LITE B4 range. The same stands for the Netmask. (default=1, )
- default_container [ string ]
Description: Container: The device or network that this element resides behind or within
- count [ number ]
Description: B4 Count: Defines the number of simulated B4 devices (min=1, max=1000000, default=1, )
- aftr_count [ number ]
Description: AFTR Count: Defines the number of AFTR devices in the topology. The implicit increment for the 'AFTR IPv6 Base Address' is 1 for each 'count'. (min=1, max=1000000, default=1, )
- host_ip_base_addr [ string ]
Description: Host IPv4 Base Address: IPv4 base address for hosts behind B4
- ip_address [ string ]
Description: B4 IPv6 Base Address: The IPv6 address for the first B4. This address will be incremented by 1 for each 'B4 Count'
- hosts_ip_increment [ string ]
Description: Subnet IPv4 Increment: This increment is only configurable if the 'Host IPv4 address allocation mode' is set to 'Static/CPE defined'. Otherwise it will be grayed-out. This increment is used only if the 'B4 Count' value is greater than 1. Example: The 'B4 Count' value is 2. The 'Host IPv4 Base Address' is 192.168.0.10. The 'Subnet IPv4 Increment' is 0.0.2.0. The 'Count' value, from the 'IPv4 STATIC HOSTS' element range which has as container this DS-LITE B4 range, is 7. The first B4 will have hosts starting with 192.168.0.10 through 192.168.0.16. The second B4 will have hosts starting with 192.168.2.10 and end up with 192.168.2.16. (default=0.0.0.1, )
- ipv6_addr_alloc_mode [ enum ]
Description: B4 IPv6 address allocation mode : Defines the way the IPv6 address is allocated. Static: the starting IPv6 address will be the one set in 'B4 IPv6 Base Address' (default=1, )
- aftr_addr [ string ]
Description: AFTR IPv6 Base Address: Defines the IPv6 address of the first AFTR device. If 'AFTR Count' is greater than 1, then the base address will be incremented with 1 for each 'count'.
- id [ string ]
Description: ID:
- gateway_ip_address [ string ]
Description: B4 Gateway IPv6 Address: Defines the IPv6 gateway address for the B4

- plmn [ string ]
Description: PLMN Settings:
- sgw_advertised_pgw [ string ]
Description: Advertised PGW Address: The simulated SGW will advertise that the MME should connect to this address for the PGW (GTP-U) connection for new sessions. Enables this secondary simulated PGW IP on the network as well.

Application Profile : 'appProfile'

Description: BPS object type: Canned or Custom.

Operations:

add( add[list])
Description: Adds a list of SuperFlow to the current working Application Profile. ([{'superflow':'adadad', 'weight':'20'},{..}])

delete( name[string])
Description: Deletes a given Application Profile from the database.
(name) = The name of the Application Profiles.

exportAppProfile( name[string], attachments[bool], filepath[string])
Description: Exports an Application profile and all of its dependencies.This operation can not be executed from the RESTApi Browser, it needs to be executed from a remote system through a REST call.
(name) = The name of the test model to be exported.
(attachments) = True if object attachments are needed.
(filepath) = The local path where to save the exported object.

saveAs( name[string], force[bool])
Description: Saves the current working Application Profiles and gives it a new name.
(name) = The new name given for the current working Application Profile
(force) = Force to save the working Application Profile using the given name.

save( name[string] = null, force[bool] = True)
Description: Saves the current working application profile using the current name. No need to use any parameter.
(name) = The name of the template. No need to configure. The current name is used.
(force) = Force to save the working Application Profile with the same name. No need to configure. The default is used.

importAppProfile( name[string], filename[string], force[bool])
Description: Imports an application profile, given as a file. This operation can not be executed from the RESTApi Browser, it needs to be executed from a remote system through a REST call.
(name) = The name of the object being imported
(filename) = The file containing the object
(force) = Force to import the file and the object having the same name will be replaced.

search( searchString[string], limit[string], sort[string], sortorder[string])
(searchString) = Search application profile name matching the string given.
(limit) = The limit of rows to return
(sort) = Parameter to sort by.
(sortorder) = The sort order (ascending/descending)

load( template[string])
Description: Load an existing Application Profile and sets it as the current one.
(template) = The name of the template application profile

new( template[string] = null)
Description: Creates a new Application Profile.
(template) = This argument must remain unset. Do not set any value for it.

remove( superflow[string])
Description: Removes a SuperFlow from the current working Application Profile.
(superflow) = The name of the super flow.

recompute( )
Description: Recompute percentages in the current working Application Profile

evasionProfile.StrikeOptions.Global
Description: Global :
Attributes:
- AllowDeprecated [ bool ]
Description: AllowDeprecated : Allow deprecated strikes to run (default=false, )
- BehaviorOnTimeout [ enum ]
Description: BehaviorOnTimeout : When using the previous timeout option for a long running strike, you can change the way that it is reported. By default it is marked as Skipped since we did not complete the sending of the attack. (default=Skipped, )
- FalsePositives [ bool ]
Description: FalsePositives : Run strikes in false positive mode (i.e. just shy of an actual attack). (default=false, )
- CachePoisoning [ enum ]
Description: CachePoisoning : Run strikes in a Cache Poisoning mode. For example, a false positive enabled attack can be run through an IPS, followed by the actual attack. This mode is useful for detailed testing of an IPS behavior. (default=Disabled, )
- MaxTimeoutPerStrike [ number ]
Description: MaxTimeoutPerStrike : Maximum time to run an individual strike. A zero means run without any timeout. On a timeout the strike will be marked as Skipped by default since we stopped short of sending all the data. Note this is only meaningful for analysis and fuzzers where a target device doesn't RST or FIN connections on purpose. This parameter is measured in seconds and ranges between 1 and 86400 seconds. (min=1, max=86400, default=0, )
- IOTimeout [ number ]
Description: I/O Timeout : Maximum time to wait for data transmission to complete. In some cases - such as large file transfers - it may be useful to set this value to a high number to prevent connection timeouts. (min=1, max=86400, default=20, )

evasionProfile.StrikeOptions.IMAP4
Description: IMAP4 :
Attributes:
- AuthenticationType [ enum ]
Description: AuthenticationType : Modify the type of IMAP4 authentication sent (default=Default, )
- IMAPUseProxyMode [ bool ]
Description: IMAPProxyRequiresEntireMessage : Sends IMAP traffic in proxy mode. Basically, this sends messages that are typically sent in multiple writes to a socket on the application layer in a single write. This is needed if the DUT expects to receive an entire response before forwarding to the other side. Normally we expect if we sent a message it should appear on the other side. This setting negates that behavior. (default=false, )
- Password [ object ]
Description: Password : Password to send in IMAP4 connections when AuthenticationType is set to user-specified (default=, )
- Username [ object ]
Description: Username : Username to send in IMAP4 connections when AuthenticationType is set to user-specified (default=, )

evasionProfile.StrikeOptions.IP
Description: IP :
Attributes:
- FragPolicy [ enum ]
Description: FragPolicy : Specify how IP fragments are reassembled. Ipv4 only (default=Last, )
- RFC3128FakePort [ number ]
Description: RFC3128FakePort : This is the destination port value to overwrite in the first fragmented SYN packet as described in RFC3128. (min=1, max=65535, default=80, )
- MaxReadSize [ number ]
Description: MaxReadSize : Maximum IP packet size for server-to-client transactions (min=8, max=65528, default=65528, )
- RFC3128 [ bool ]
Description: RFC3128 : Use a different TCP port number for first fragmented packet, as described in RFC3128. (default=false, )
- TTL [ number ]
Description: TTL : Maximum IP Time to Live (min=1, max=255, default=255, )
- MaxFragSize [ number ]
Description: MaxFragSize : Maximum IP packet size for all transactions (min=8, max=65528, default=65528, )
- FragOrder [ enum ]
Description: FragOrder : Change the order in which fragments are sent. Ipv4 only (default=default, )
- TOS [ number ]
Description: TOS : Configure the TOS field used for all IP packets (min=0, max=255, default=0, )
- IPEvasionsOnBothSides [ bool ]
Description: IPEvasionsOnBothSides : Allow use of IP Evasions on both sides, regardless of Strike direction (default=false, )
- RFC3514 [ bool ]
Description: RFC3514 : Enable RFC3514 compatibility (default=false, )
- ReadWriteWindowSize [ number ]
Description: ReadWriteWindowSize : This setting dictates how many bytes of data the client and the server may read or write from a TCP/UDP socket. This is useful when running over a proxy that process an entire response, for example, the client sends and HTTP GET and the server responds with a 400MB file, but none of this data is sent to the client side until the proxy downloads and scans the entire 400MB contents, then sends it on to the client. (max=1073741824, default=65535, )
- MaxWriteSize [ number ]
Description: MaxWriteSize : Maximum IP packet size for client-to-server transactions (min=8, max=65528, default=65528, )
- FragEvasion [ enum ]
Description: FragEvasion : Enable IP evasion using fragmentation (default=Disabled, )

evasionProfile.StrikeOptions.SMTP
Description: SMTP :
Attributes:
- ShuffleHeaders [ bool ]
Description: ShuffleHeaders : Randomize the order of the SMTP headers (default=false, )
- SMTPUseProxyMode [ bool ]
Description: SMTPProxyRequiresEntireMessage : Sends SMTP traffic in proxy mode. Basically, this sends messages that are typically sent in multiple writes to a socket on the application layer in a single write. This is needed if the DUT expects to receive an entire response before forwarding to the other side. Normally we expect if we sent a message it should appear on the other side. This setting negates that behavior. (default=false, )
- PadCommandWhitespace [ bool ]
Description: PadCommandWhitespace : Use space and tab characters to pad the whitespace between commands and arguments (default=false, )
